WHEN TO USE\n28: \n29: ### When to Use This Skill\n30: \n31: Use this skill when:\n32: - Deep investigation requiring multiple rounds of discovery\n33: - Topic spans 3+ technical domains or sources\n34: - Initial findings need progressive refinement\n35: - Overnight or unattended research sessions\n36: - Research where prior findings inform subsequent queries\n37: \n38: ### When NOT to Use\n39: \n40: - Simple, single-question research (use direct codebase search or `/spec_kit:plan`)\n41: - Known-solution documentation (use `/spec_kit:plan`)\n42: - Implementation tasks (use `/spec_kit:implement`)\n43: - Quick codebase searches (use `@context` or direct Grep/Glob)\n44: - Fewer than 3 sources needed (single-pass research suffices)\n45: \n46: ### FORBIDDEN INVOCATION PATTERNS\n47: \n48: This skill is invoked EXCLUSIVELY through the `/spec_kit:deep-research` command. The command's YAML workflow owns state, dispatch, and convergence.\n49: \n50: **NEVER:**\n51: - Write a custom bash/shell dispatcher to parallelize iterations\n52: - Invoke cli-codex / cli-gemini / cli-claude-code directly in a loop to simulate iterations\n53: - Manually write iteration prompts to `/tmp` and dispatch them via `copilot -p`\n54: - Dispatch the `@deep-research` LEAF agent via the Task tool for iteration loops (the agent is LEAF — a single iteration — and MUST be driven by the command's workflow)\n55: - Skip the state machine: `deep-research-state.jsonl`, `deep-research-config.json`, `deltas/`, `prompts/`, `logs/`\n56: - Manage iteration state outside the resolved local research packet under `{spec_folder}/research/`\n57: \n58: **ALWAYS:**\n59: - Invoke via `/spec_kit:deep-research:auto` or `/spec_kit:deep-research:confirm`\n60: - Let the command's YAML workflow own dispatch (auto: `.opencode/commands/spec_kit/assets/spec_kit_deep-research_auto.yaml`)\n61: - Let `scripts/reduce-state.cjs` be the SINGLE state writer\n62: - Require every iteration to produce BOTH the markdown narrative AND the JSONL delta (dispatch scripts must fail if either is missing)\n63: - Use `resolveArtifactRoot(specFolder, 'research')` from `.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/shared/review-research-paths.cjs` to locate the canonical research root\n64: \n65: ### Executor Selection Contract\n66: \n67: The YAML workflow owns executor selection. Native `@deep-research` is the default path; CLI executors are routed through the workflow, not through ad hoc shell loops.\n68: \n69: Cross-CLI delegation is possible inside each executor sandbox but discouraged. Do not invoke the same CLI from within itself, and do not assume auth from a parent executor propagates to child CLIs.\n70: \n71: **Invariants** the executor MUST satisfy regardless of route:\n72: \n73: 1. Produce an iteration markdown file at `{state_paths.iteration_pattern}` (non-empty).\n74: 2. Append a JSONL delta record to `{state_paths.state_log}` with required fields: `type`, `iteration`, `newInfoRatio`, `status`, `focus`. Optional: `graphEvents`.\n75: 3. Respect the LEAF-agent constraint: no sub-dispatch, no nested loops. Max 12 tool calls per iteration.\n76: \n77: **Failure modes**:\n78: \n79: - Missing iteration file → `iteration_file_missing` from `post-dispatch-validate.ts`, emits `schema_mismatch` conflict event.\n80: - Empty iteration file → `iteration_file_empty`, same downstream.\n81: - JSONL not appended → `jsonl_not_appended`.\n82: - JSONL missing required fields → `jsonl_missing_fields`.\n83: - JSONL malformed → `jsonl_parse_error`.\n84: - 3 consecutive failures → existing `stuck_recovery` event (unchanged).\n85: \n86: **JSONL audit field**: Non-native executor runs append executor metadata (`model`, effort, tier) to the iteration's JSONL record via `executor-audit.ts`. Native runs are recoverable from YAML alone.\n87: \n88: **Template**: The executor-agnostic iteration prompt lives at `.opencode/skills/deep-research/assets/prompt_pack_iteration.md.tmpl`. It is rendered by `prompt-pack.ts` before dispatch and either (a) injected as the agent's context (native) or (b) piped to `codex exec` stdin (cli-codex).\n89: \n90: **Config surface**: Defined in `assets/deep_research_config.json` under the `executor` key. Schema is in `.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/lib/deep-loop/executor-config.ts`. CLI flag precedence is: `--executor/--model/--reasoning-effort/--service-tier/--executor-timeout > config file > schema default`.\n91: \n92: **What NEVER changes regardless of executor route**:\n93: \n94: - YAML owns state (`deep-research-state.jsonl`, strategy.md, registry, dashboard).\n95: - `reduce-state.cjs` is the single state writer.\n96: - Convergence detection, lifecycle events (new/resume/restart), and stuck_recovery all stay YAML-driven.\n97: - The `@deep-research` LEAF agent definition is untouched — it is the native executor, not the only one.\n98: \n99: ### Code-Graph Readiness TrustState Surface\n100: \n101: On this skill surface, the live code-graph readiness contract only reaches four TrustState values: `live`, `stale`, `absent`, and `unavailable`.\n102: \n103: `cached`, `imported`, `rebuilt`, and `rehomed` remain declared in the shared TrustState type for compatibility and downstream schema stability, but the seven code-graph handlers and readiness helpers used here do not emit them today.\n104: \n105: ### Keyword Triggers\n106: \n107: `autoresearch`, `deep research`, `autonomous research`, `research loop`, `iterative research`, `multi-round research`, `deep investigation`, `comprehensive research`\n108: \n109: For iterative code review and quality auditing, see `deep-review`.\n110: \n111: ### Lifecycle Contract\n112: \n113: Runtime-supported lifecycle modes (current release):\n114: - `new` — first run against the spec folder\n115: - `resume` — continue the active lineage; appends a typed `resumed` JSONL event with `sessionId`, `parentSessionId`, `lineageMode`, `continuedFromRun`, `generation`, `archivedPath` (null), and `timestamp`\n116: - `restart` — archive the existing `research/` tree under `research_archive/{timestamp}/`, mint a fresh `sessionId`, increment `generation`, and append a typed `restarted` JSONL event with the same field set plus a non-null `archivedPath`\n117: \n118: Deferred (reserved, not runtime-supported):\n119: - `fork` — earlier drafts described a sibling-lineage branch; the workflow no longer exposes this as an option\n120: - `completed-continue` — earlier drafts described snapshotting the prior synthesis as immutable `synthesis-v{generation}.md`; not runtime-wired\n121: \n122: See `references/loop_protocol.md §Lifecycle Branches` for the canonical event contract and the rationale for the retraction.\n123: \n124: ---\n125: \n126: ## 2. SMART ROUTING\n127: \n128: \n129: ### Resource Loading Levels\n130: \n131: | Level | When to Load | Resources |\n132: |-------|-------------|-----------|\n133: | ALWAYS | Every skill invocation | Quick reference baseline |\n134: | CONDITIONAL | If intent signals match | Loop protocol, convergence, state format |\n135: | ON_DEMAND | Only on explicit request | Templates, detailed specifications |\n136: \n137: ### Smart Router Pseudocode\n138: \n139: - Pattern 1: Runtime Discovery - `discover_markdown_resources()` recursively scans `references/` and `assets/`.\n140: - Pattern 2: Existence-Check Before Load - `load_if_available()` uses `_guard_in_skill()`, `inventory`, and `seen`.\n141: - Pattern 3: Extensible Routing Key - setup, iteration, convergence, and state intents route loop resources.\n142: - Pattern 4: Multi-Tier Graceful Fallback - `UNKNOWN_FALLBACK` asks for loop/setup/state disambiguation and missing intent routes return a \"no knowledge base\" notice.\n143: \n144: ```python\n145: from pathlib import Path\n146: \n147: SKILL_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parent\n148: RESOURCE_BASES = (SKILL_ROOT / \"references\", SKILL_ROOT / \"assets\")\n149: DEFAULT_RESOURCE = \"references/quick_reference.md\"\n150: \n151: INTENT_SIGNALS = {\n152:     \"LOOP_SETUP\": {\"weight\": 4, \"keywords\": [\"autoresearch\", \"deep research\", \"research loop\", \"autonomous research\"]},\n153:     \"ITERATION\": {\"weight\": 4, \"keywords\": [\"iteration\", \"next round\", \"continue research\", \"research cycle\"]},\n154:     \"CONVERGENCE\": {\"weight\": 3, \"keywords\": [\"convergence\", \"stop condition\", \"diminishing returns\", \"stuck\"]},\n155:     \"STATE\": {\"weight\": 3, \"keywords\": [\"state file\", \"JSONL\", \"strategy\", \"resume\", \"auto-resume\"]},\n156: }\n157: \n158: NOISY_SYNONYMS = {\n159:     \"LOOP_SETUP\": {\"run research\": 2.0, \"investigate deeply\": 1.8, \"overnight research\": 1.5},\n160:     \"ITERATION\": {\"another pass\": 1.5, \"keep searching\": 1.4, \"dig deeper\": 1.6},\n161:     \"CONVERGENCE\": {\"good enough\": 1.4, \"stop when\": 1.5, \"diminishing\": 1.6},\n162:     \"STATE\": {\"pick up where\": 1.5, \"continue from\": 1.4, \"resume\": 1.8},\n163: }\n164: \n165: RESOURCE_MAP = {\n166:     \"LOOP_SETUP\": [\"references/loop_protocol.md\", \"references/state_format.md\", \"assets/deep_research_config.json\"],\n167:     \"ITERATION\": [\"references/loop_protocol.md\", \"references/convergence.md\"],\n168:     \"CONVERGENCE\": [\"references/convergence.md\"],\n169:     \"STATE\": [\"references/state_format.md\", \"assets/deep_research_strategy.md\"],\n170: }\n171: \n172: LOADING_LEVELS = {\n173:     \"ALWAYS\": [DEFAULT_RESOURCE],\n174:     \"ON_DEMAND_KEYWORDS\": [\"full protocol\", \"all templates\", \"complete reference\", \"resume deep research\", \"routing-accuracy iteration\", \"state log\", \"research/iterations\", \"deltas\", \"overnight research\", \"active lineage\"],\n175:     \"ON_DEMAND\": [\"references/loop_protocol.md\", \"references/state_format.md\", \"references/convergence.md\"],\n176: }\n177: ```\n178: \n179: ### Scoped Guard and Loading\n180: \n181: ```python\n182: UNKNOWN_FALLBACK = [\"Confirm setup vs iteration vs convergence vs state recovery\", \"Confirm spec folder and research packet\"]\n183: \n184: def _guard_in_skill(relative_path: str) -> str:\n185:     resolved = (SKILL_ROOT / relative_path).resolve()\n186:     resolved.relative_to(SKILL_ROOT)\n187:     if resolved.suffix.lower() != \".md\":\n188:         raise ValueError(f\"Only markdown resources are routable: {relative_path}\")\n189:     return resolved.relative_to(SKILL_ROOT).as_posix()\n190: \n191: def discover_markdown_resources() -> set[str]:\n192:     docs = []\n193:     for base in RESOURCE_BASES:\n194:         if base.exists():\n195:             docs.extend(p for p in base.rglob(\"*.md\") if p.is_file())\n196:     return {doc.relative_to(SKILL_ROOT).as_posix() for doc in docs}\n197: \n198: def load_if_available(relative_path: str) -> None:\n199:     guarded = _guard_in_skill(relative_path)\n200:     if guarded in inventory and guarded not in seen:\n201:         load(guarded)\n202:         seen.add(guarded)\n203: ```\n204: \n205: ### Phase Detection\n206: \n207: Detect the current research phase from dispatch context to load appropriate resources:\n208: \n209: | Phase | Signal | Resources to Load |\n210: |-------|--------|-------------------|\n211: | Init | No JSONL exists | Loop protocol, state format |\n212: | Iteration | Dispatch context includes iteration number | Loop protocol, convergence |\n213: | Stuck | Dispatch context includes \"RECOVERY\" | Convergence, loop protocol |\n214: | Synthesis | Convergence triggered STOP | Quick reference |\n215: \n216: ---\n217: \n218: ## 3. HOW IT WORKS\n219: \n220: ### Resource Map Integration\n221: \n222: When `{spec_folder}/resource-map.md` exists at init, deep research promotes it from ad hoc context to canonical packet state.\n223: \n224: - Persist `resource_map_present: true` in `deep-research-config.json`.\n225: - Read the map once during init and summarize it into `deep-research-strategy.md` `Known Context`.\n226: - The snapshot MUST include per-section entry counts across `READMEs`, `Documents`, `Commands`, `Agents`, `Skills`, `Specs`, `Scripts`, `Tests`, `Config`, and `Meta`.\n227: - The snapshot MUST also include a one-line theme summary for each resource-map section so later iterations inherit the map's structure without rereading the entire file.\n228: - Per-iteration prompts surface `resource-map.md` as the exclusion set for previously inventoried files.\n229: - Treat files already listed on the map as known inventory, not as net-new discoveries.\n230: - Only flag files as gaps when they look relevant to the active investigation and are missing from the map.\n231: - Final synthesis cites `{spec_folder}/resource-map.md` in `research.md` References when the map was present at init.\n232: - Convergence also emits `{artifact_dir}/resource-map.md` from research delta evidence unless the operator passes `--no-resource-map`.\n233: \n234: When `{spec_folder}/resource-map.md` is absent at init:\n235: \n236: - Persist `resource_map_present: false`.\n237: - Write `resource-map.md not present; skipping coverage gate` into `Known Context`.\n238: - Omit the exclusion-set hint from iteration guidance.\n239: - Continue the loop normally; absence is informational, not a failure.\n240: \n241: ### Architecture: 3-Layer Integration\n242: \n243: `/spec_kit:deep-research` owns the YAML workflow, which initializes state, dispatches one LEAF iteration at a time, evaluates convergence, synthesizes `research/research.md`, and saves continuity. The `@deep-research` agent executes only one research cycle per dispatch.\n244: \n245: ### State Packet Location\n246: \n247: The research state packet always lives under the target spec's local `research/` folder. Root-spec targets use `{spec_folder}/research/` directly. Child-phase and sub-phase targets use **flat-first**: a first run with an empty `research/` directory writes flat at `{spec_folder}/research/`. A `pt-NN` subfolder (`{basename(spec_folder)}-pt-{NN}`) is allocated only when prior content already exists in `research/` for a non-matching target (continuation runs reuse the existing flat artifact or matching `pt-NN` packet). This avoids the unnecessary `pt-01` wrapper on first runs.\n248: \n249: Example (first run on a child phase): `.../026-graph.../019-system-hardening/001-initial-research/004-desc-regen/` → `004-desc-regen/research/` (flat, no subfolder).\n250: \n251: Example (subsequent run with prior content for a different target): `004-desc-regen/research/004-desc-regen-pt-02/` (pt-NN allocated as a sibling to the prior content).\n252: \n253: State files include `deep-research-config.json`, `deep-research-state.jsonl`, `deep-research-strategy.md`, `findings-registry.json`, `deep-research-dashboard.md`, `.deep-research-pause`, `.deep-research.lock`, `resource-map.md`, `research.md`, and `iterations/iteration-NNN.md`.\n254: \n255: ### Core Innovation: Fresh Context Per Iteration\n256: \n257: Each agent dispatch gets a fresh context window. State continuity comes from files, not memory. This solves context degradation in long research sessions.\n258: \n259: Adapted from: karpathy/autoresearch (loop concept), AGR (fresh context \"Ralph Loop\"), pi-autoresearch (JSONL state), autoresearch-opencode (context injection).\n260: \n261: ### Data Flow\n262: \n263: Init creates config, strategy, and state logs. Each loop reads state, checks convergence, dispatches `@deep-research`, writes iteration markdown and JSONL deltas, refreshes reducer-owned state, and either continues or synthesizes and saves continuity.\n264: \n265: Late-INIT can also anchor the research run to `spec.md`: the workflow acquires the advisory lock, classifies `folder_state`, seeds or appends bounded context before LOOP, and then syncs one generated findings block back into `spec.md` during SYNTHESIS while keeping `research/research.md` canonical.\n266: \n267: That contract is exact:\n268: - `folder_state` is always one of `no-spec`, `spec-present`, `spec-just-created-by-this-run`, or `conflict-detected`\n269: - the advisory lock lives at `research/.deep-research.lock` from late INIT through save, skip-save, or cancel cleanup\n270: - post-synthesis write-back replaces exactly one `<!-- BEGIN GENERATED: deep-research/spec-findings -->` ... `<!-- END GENERATED: deep-research/spec-findings -->` fence under the chosen host anchor\n271: - the full bounded mutation rules live in [spec_check_protocol.md](references/spec_check_protocol.md)\n272: \n273: ### Key Concepts\n274: \n275: Research continuity is externalized to files, each iteration starts fresh, convergence uses newInfoRatio/stuck/question signals, strategy and registry are reducer-owned, JSONL remains append-only, and final synthesis consolidates `research/research.md`.\n276: \n277: ---\n278: \n279: ## 4. RULES\n280: \n281: ### ✅ ALWAYS\n282: \n283: 1. **Read state first** -- Agent must read JSONL and strategy.md before any research action\n284: 2. **One focus per iteration** -- Pick ONE research sub-topic from strategy.md \"Next Focus\"\n285: 3. **Externalize findings** -- Write to iteration-NNN.md, not held in agent context\n286: 4. **Update strategy** -- Append to \"What Worked\"/\"What Failed\", update \"Next Focus\"\n287: 5. **Report newInfoRatio** -- Every iteration JSONL record must include newInfoRatio\n288: 6. **Respect exhausted approaches** -- Never retry approaches in the \"Exhausted\" list\n289: 7. **Cite sources** -- Every finding must cite `[SOURCE: url]` or `[SOURCE: file:line]`\n290: 8. **Use generate-context.js for memory saves** -- Never manually create memory files\n291: 9. **Treat research/research.md as workflow-owned** -- Iteration findings feed synthesis; the workflow owns the canonical `research/research.md`\n292: 10. **Document ruled-out directions per iteration** -- Every iteration must include what was tried and failed\n293: 11. **Report newInfoRatio + 1-sentence novelty justification** -- Every JSONL iteration record must include both\n294: 12. **Quality guards must pass before convergence** -- Source diversity, focus alignment, and no single-weak-source checks must pass before STOP can trigger\n295: 13. **Respect reducer ownership** -- The workflow reducer, not the agent, is the source of truth for strategy machine-owned sections, dashboard metrics, and findings registry updates\n296: 14. **Use canonical packet names only** -- Write `deep-research-*` artifacts and `research/.deep-research-pause`; legacy names are read-only migration aliases\n297: \n298: ### ❌ NEVER\n299: \n300: 1. **Dispatch sub-agents** -- @deep-research is LEAF-only (NDP compliance)\n301: 2. **Hold findings in context** -- Write everything to files\n302: 3. **Exceed TCB** -- Target 8-11 tool calls per iteration (max 12)\n303: 4. **Ask the user** -- Autonomous execution; make best-judgment decisions\n304: 5. **Skip convergence checks** -- Every iteration must be evaluated\n305: 6. **Modify config after init** -- Config is read-only after initialization\n306: 7. **Overwrite prior findings** -- Append to research/research.md, never replace\n307: 8. **Implement fixes during research** -- Report findings only; implementation is a separate follow-up step.\n308: \n309: ### Iteration Status Enum\n310: \n311: `complete | timeout | error | stuck | insight | thought`\n312: \n313: - `insight`: Low newInfoRatio but important conceptual breakthrough\n314: - `thought`: Analytical-only iteration, no evidence gathering\n315: \n316: ### EXPERIMENTAL / REFERENCE-ONLY FEATURES\n317: \n318: These concepts remain documented for future design work, but they are not part of the live executable contract for `/spec_kit:deep-research`:\n319: 1. **Wave orchestration** -- parallel question fan-out, pruning, and breakthrough logic\n320: 2. **Checkpoint commits** -- per-iteration git commits\n321: 3. **Wave orchestration on the same lineage** -- parallel fan-out remains reference-only\n322: 4. **Alternate CLI dispatch** -- process-isolated `claude -p` or similar dispatch modes\n323: \n324: ### ⚠️ ESCALATE IF\n325: \n326: 1. **3+ consecutive timeouts** -- Infrastructure issue, not research problem\n327: 2. **State file corruption unrecoverable** -- Cannot reconstruct from JSONL or iteration files\n328: 3. **All approaches exhausted with questions remaining** -- Research may need human guidance\n329: 4. **Security concern in findings** -- Proprietary code or credentials discovered\n330: 5. **All recovery tiers exhausted** -- No automatic recovery path remaining\n331: \n332: ---\n333: \n334: ## 5. REFERENCES\n335: \n336: Core documentation: `references/loop_protocol.md`, `references/spec_check_protocol.md`, `references/state_format.md`, `references/convergence.md`, and `references/quick_reference.md`.\n337: \n338: Templates: `assets/deep_research_config.json`, `assets/deep_research_strategy.md`, and `assets/deep_research_dashboard.md`.\n339: \n340: ---\n341: \n342: ## 6. SUCCESS CRITERIA\n343: \n344: ### Loop Completion\n345: - Research loop ran to convergence or max iterations\n346: - All state files present and consistent (config, JSONL, strategy)\n347: - research/resource-map.md produced from converged deltas unless `config.resource_map.emit == false` (operator flag: `--no-resource-map`)\n348: - research/research.md produced with findings from all iterations\n349: - Canonical continuity surfaces updated via generate-context.js\n350: \n351: ### Quality Gates\n352: \n353: Blocking gates: valid config/strategy/state before loop, iteration markdown plus JSONL plus reducer refresh per iteration, final `research/research.md` and convergence report after loop, and quality guards for source diversity/focus/no weak single source. Continuity save is expected but non-blocking.\n354: \n355: ### Convergence Report\n356: \n357: Every completed loop produces a convergence report:\n358: - Stop reason (converged, max_iterations, all_questions_answered, stuck_unrecoverable)\n359: - Total iterations completed\n360: - Questions answered ratio\n361: - Average newInfoRatio trend\n362: \n363: ---\n364: \n365: ## 7. INTEGRATION POINTS\n366: \n367: ### Framework Integration\n368: \n369: This skill operates within the behavioral framework defined in the active runtime's root doc (CLAUDE.md, AGENTS.md, CODEX.md, or GEMINI.md).\n370: \n371: Key integrations:\n372: - **Gate 2**: Skill routing via `skill_advisor.py` (keywords: autoresearch, deep research)\n373: - **Gate 3**: File modifications require spec folder question per the root doc Gate 3\n374: - **Continuity**: `/spec_kit:resume` is the operator-facing recovery surface; canonical packet continuity is written via `generate-context.js`\n375: - **Orchestrator**: @orchestrate dispatches @deep-research as LEAF agent\n376: \n377: ### Continuity Integration\n378: \n379: Before research, recover context with `/spec_kit:resume` using `handover.md -> _memory.continuity -> spec docs`. SMART ROUTING\n117: \n118: \n119: ### Resource Loading Levels\n120: \n121: | Level | When to Load | Resources |\n122: |-------|-------------|-----------|\n123: | ALWAYS | Every skill invocation | `get_routing_key()` derives the review phase from dispatch context.\n132: - Pattern 4: Multi-Tier Graceful Fallback - `UNKNOWN_FALLBACK` returns review disambiguation and missing phases return a \"no review resources\" notice.\n133: \n134: ```python\n135: from pathlib import Path\n136: \n137: SKILL_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parent\n138: RESOURCE_BASES = (SKILL_ROOT / \"references\", / relative_path).resolve()\n205:     resolved.relative_to(SKILL_ROOT)\n206:     if resolved.suffix.lower() != \".md\":\n207:         raise ValueError(f\"Only markdown resources are routable: {relative_path}\")\n208:     return resolved.relative_to(SKILL_ROOT).as_posix()\n209: \n210: def discover_markdown_resources() -> set[str]:\n211:     docs = []\n212:     for base in phase\n221:     text = str(getattr(dispatch_context, \"text\", \"\")).lower()\n222:     if \"recovery\" in text:\n223:         return \"stuck\"\n224:     if \"convergence\" in text or \"synthesis\" in LOADING_LEVELS[\"ON_DEMAND_KEYWORDS\"]):\n275:         for relative_path in LOADING_LEVELS[\"ON_DEMAND\"]:\n276:             load_if_available(relative_path)\n277: \n278:     return {\n279:         \"routing_key\": routing_key,\n280:         \"intents\": intents,\n281:         \"resources\": loaded,\n282:         \"non_markdown_references\": NON_MARKDOWN_REFERENCES,\n283:     }\n284: ```\n285: \n286: ### Phase Detection\n287: \n288: Detect the current review phase from dispatch context to load appropriate resources:\n289: \n290: | Phase | Signal | Resources to Load |\n291: |-------|--------|-------------------|\n292: | Init | No JSONL exists in `review/` | Loop protocol, state format, review contract |\n293: | Iteration | Dispatch context includes dimension + iteration number | Loop protocol, convergence, review contract |\n294: | Stuck | Dispatch context includes \"RECOVERY\" | Convergence, loop protocol |\n295: | Synthesis | Convergence triggered STOP | Review contract, state format |\n296: \n297: ---\n298: \n299: ## 3. HOW IT WORKS\n300: \n301: ### Resource Map Coverage Gate\n302: \n303: When `{spec_folder}/resource-map.md` exists at init, deep review treats it as a first-class audit input instead of optional prompt wiring.\n304: \n305: - Persist `resource_map_present: true` in `deep-review-config.json`.\n306: - Add a resource-map snapshot to `Known Context` so later iterations inherit the packet inventory baseline.\n307: - Promote `Resource Map Coverage` to a first-class audit angle alongside correctness, regression risk, test coverage, cross-runtime parity, observability, and docs-vs-code drift.\n308: - Reserve at least one loop iteration to cross-check `target_files` from `{spec_folder}/applied/T-*.md` against `resource-map.md`.\n309: - Treat that pass as mandatory coverage work, not an optional traceability extra.\n310: - Classify results into three buckets: entries touched, entries not touched (`expected-by-scope` vs `gap`), and implementation paths absent from the map.\n311: - Findings emitted from that audit use the `resource-map-coverage` category.\n312: - Synthesis inserts `## Resource Map Coverage Gate` into `review-report.md` when the map was present at init.\n313: - Convergence also emits `{artifact_dir}/resource-map.md` from review delta evidence unless the operator passes `--no-resource-map`.\n314: \n315: When `{spec_folder}/resource-map.md` is absent at init:\n316: \n317: - Persist `resource_map_present: false`.\n318: - Log `resource-map.md not present; skipping coverage gate` in `Known Context`.\n319: - Skip the coverage-gate pass and omit the report section without failing the loop.\n320: \n321: ### Architecture\n322: \n323: `/spec_kit:deep-review` owns the loop. The YAML workflow initializes state, dispatches one LEAF review iteration at a time, evaluates convergence, synthesizes `review-report.md`, and saves continuity. The LEAF agent reads state, reviews one dimension, writes `iteration-NNN.md`, updates strategy, and appends JSONL.\n324: \n325: ### State Packet Location\n326: \n327: The review state packet always lives under the target spec's local `review/` folder. Root-spec targets use `{spec_folder}/review/` directly. Child-phase and sub-phase targets use **flat-first**: a first run with an empty `review/` directory writes flat at `{spec_folder}/review/`. A `pt-NN` subfolder (`{basename(spec_folder)}-pt-{NN}`) is allocated only when prior content already exists in `review/` for a non-matching target (continuation runs reuse the existing flat artifact or matching `pt-NN` packet). This avoids the unnecessary `pt-01` wrapper on first runs.\n328: \n329: Example (first run on a child phase): `.../026-graph.../006-continuity-refactor-gates/003-gate-c-writer-ready/` → `003-gate-c-writer-ready/review/` (flat, no subfolder).\n330: \n331: Example (subsequent run with prior content for a different target): `003-gate-c-writer-ready/review/003-gate-c-writer-ready-pt-02/` (pt-NN allocated as a sibling to the prior content).\n332: \n333: Core artifacts: `deep-review-config.json`, `deep-review-state.jsonl`, `deep-review-strategy.md`, `deep-review-dashboard.md`, `.deep-review-pause`, `resource-map.md`, `review-report.md`, and `iterations/iteration-NNN.md`.\n334: \n335: ### Core Innovation: Fresh Context Per Iteration\n336: \n337: Each agent dispatch gets a fresh context window. State continuity comes from files, not memory. This solves context degradation in long review sessions where accumulated findings would otherwise bias subsequent dimensions.\n338: \n339: ### Data Flow\n340: \n341: Init creates config, strategy, and JSONL state. Each loop reads state, checks convergence, dispatches one dimension, records findings, and reduces state. Synthesis compiles the final report and saves continuity.\n342: \n343: ### Review Dimensions\n344: \n345: The four primary review dimensions (configured in `assets/review_mode_contract.yaml`):\n346: \n347: | Dimension | Focus | Key Questions |\n348: |-----------|-------|---------------|\n349: | **Correctness** | Logic, behavior, error handling | Does the code do what it claims? Are edge cases handled? |\n350: | **Security** | Vulnerabilities, exposure, trust boundaries | Are inputs validated? Are credentials exposed? |\n351: | **Spec-Alignment / Traceability** | Spec vs. implementation fidelity | Does code match spec.md? Are all planned items present? |\n352: | **Completeness / Maintainability** | Coverage, dead code, documentation | Are TODOs resolved? Is the code self-documenting? |\n353: \n354: ### Lifecycle + Reducer Contract\n355: \n356: Review mode is lineage-aware. Supported lifecycle modes are `new`, `resume`, and `restart`; required lineage fields include `sessionId`, `parentSessionId`, `lineageMode`, `generation`, `continuedFromRun`, and `releaseReadinessState`. The reducer consumes the latest JSONL delta, the new iteration file, and prior reduced state, then emits finding registry, dashboard metrics, and strategy updates.\n357: \n358: ### Severity Classification\n359: \n360: | Severity | Criteria | Blocking |\n361: |----------|----------|---------|\n362: | **P0** | Correctness failure, security vulnerability, spec contradiction | Yes — blocks PASS verdict |\n363: | **P1** | Degraded behavior, incomplete implementation, missing validation | Conditional — triggers CONDITIONAL verdict |\n364: | **P2** | Style, naming, minor improvements, documentation gaps | No — PASS with advisories |\n365: \n366: ### Verdicts\n367: \n368: | Verdict | Condition |\n369: |---------|-----------|\n370: | **PASS** | No P0/P1 findings; P2 findings recorded as advisories (`hasAdvisories: true`) |\n371: | **CONDITIONAL** | P1 findings present; remediation plan included in report |\n372: | **FAIL** | Any P0 finding confirmed after adversarial self-check |\n373: \n374: ### Iteration Final-Line Contract (MANDATORY)\n375: \n376: Every `iteration-NNN.md` MUST end with exactly one of the following plain-text lines as the **absolute final line** (no trailing whitespace, no variation):\n377: \n378: ```\n379: Review verdict: PASS\n380: ```\n381: \n382: ```\n383: Review verdict: CONDITIONAL\n384: ```\n385: \n386: ```\n387: Review verdict: FAIL\n388: ```\n389: \n390: **Mapping rule:** PASS if no P0 or P1 findings in this iteration; CONDITIONAL if any P1 (but no P0) findings; FAIL if any P0 findings. P2-only findings → PASS.\n391: \n392: Downstream automation (including the synthesis phase and CI gate parser) parses this final line via exact string match — do not vary the format.\n393: \n394: ---\n395: \n396: ## 4. RULES\n397: \n398: ### ✅ ALWAYS\n399: \n400: 1. Read JSONL and strategy before review action.\n401: 2. Review one dimension per iteration and write findings to `iteration-NNN.md`.\n402: 3. Append JSONL with severity counts, finding detail, and `newInfoRatio`.\n403: 4. Cite every finding with `[SOURCE: file:line]`; reject inference-only findings.\n404: 5. Re-read cited code before recording any P0.\n405: 6. Keep target files read-only.\n406: 7. Use `generate-context.js` for continuity saves.\n407: 8. Emit setup `BINDING:` lines before workflow output.\n408: 9. Refuse nested dispatch with: `REFUSE: nested Task tool dispatch is forbidden for LEAF agents. Returning partial findings instead.`\n409: \n410: ### ❌ NEVER\n411: \n412: 1. **Dispatch sub-agents** — `@deep-review` is LEAF-only; it cannot dispatch additional agents. When dispatch is requested, use the canonical REFUSE wording (ALWAYS rule 14).\n413: 2. **Hold findings in context** — Write everything to iteration files; context is discarded after each dispatch.\n414: 3. **Exceed TCB** — Target 8-11 tool calls per iteration (max 12); breadth over depth per cycle.\n415: 4. **Ask the user** — Autonomous execution; the agent makes best-judgment decisions without pausing.\n416: 5. **Skip convergence checks** — Every iteration must be evaluated against convergence criteria before the next dispatch.\n417: 6. **Modify config after init** — `deep-review-config.json` is read-only after initialization.\n418: 7. **Modify files under review** — The review loop is observation-only; no code changes during audit.\n419: 8. **Use WebFetch** — Review is code-only; no external resource fetching is permitted.\n420: 9. **Implement fixes during review** — Report findings only; implementation is a separate follow-up step.\n421: \n422: ### Iteration Status Enum\n423: \n424: `complete | timeout | error | stuck | insight`\n425: \n426: - `insight`: Low newInfoRatio but important finding that changes the verdict trajectory.\n427: \n428: ### ⚠️ ESCALATE IF\n429: \n430: 1. **3+ consecutive timeouts** — Infrastructure issue; pause loop and report to user.\n431: 2. **State file corruption** — Cannot reconstruct iteration history from JSONL or iteration files.\n432: 3. **All dimensions covered with P0 findings remaining** — Human sign-off required before shipping.\n433: 4. **Security vulnerabilities discovered in production code** — Escalate immediately; do not defer to report synthesis.\n434: 5. **All recovery tiers exhausted** — No automatic recovery path remaining in convergence protocol.\n435: \n436: ---\n437: \n438: ## 5. REFERENCES\n439: \n440: The router discovers markdown references dynamically. Primary docs: `references/quick_reference.md`, `references/loop_protocol.md`, `references/state_format.md`, and `references/convergence.md`. Local assets provide config, strategy, dashboard, and review contract templates.\n441: \n442: ---\n443: \n444: ## 6. SUCCESS CRITERIA\n445: \n446: ### Loop Completion\n447: \n448: - Review loop ran to convergence or max iterations\n449: - All configured review dimensions have at least one iteration of coverage\n450: - All state files present and consistent (`config.json`, `state.jsonl`, `strategy.md`)\n451: - `review/resource-map.md` produced from converged deltas unless `config.resource_map.emit == false` (operator flag: `--no-resource-map`)\n452: - `review/review-report.md` produced with all 9 core sections, plus `## Resource Map Coverage Gate` when `resource_map_present == true`\n453: - Canonical continuity surfaces updated via `generate-context.js`\n454: \n455: Quality gates require valid config, initialized strategy, state log, per-iteration markdown and JSONL, final report, evidence completeness, scope alignment, severity coverage, and P0 adversarial recheck.\n456: \n457: The final report records stop reason, iteration count, dimension coverage, severity counts, verdict, and release-readiness state.\n458: \n459: ---\n460: \n461: ## 7. INTEGRATION POINTS\n462: \n463: ### Framework Integration\n464: \n465: This skill operates within the behavioral framework defined in the active runtime's root doc (CLAUDE.md, AGENTS.md, CODEX.md, or GEMINI.md).\n466: \n467: Key integrations:\n468: - **Gate 2**: Skill routing via `skill_advisor.py` (keywords: deep review, code audit, iterative review)\n469: - **Gate 3**: File modifications require spec folder question per the root doc Gate 3; the spec folder determines the `{spec_folder}/review/` state packet location\n470: - **Continuity**: `/spec_kit:resume` is the operator-facing recovery surface; canonical packet continuity is written via `generate-context.js`\n471: - **Command**: `/spec_kit:deep-review` is the primary invocation point\n472: \n473: ### Continuity Integration\n474: \n475: Recover context via `/spec_kit:resume` in the order `handover.md -> _memory.continuity -> spec docs`. During review, the agent writes iteration, strategy, and JSONL state. After synthesis, run `generate-context.js`.\n476: \n477: ### CocoIndex Integration\n478: \n479: `mcp__cocoindex_code__search` is available to `@deep-review` for semantic code search when Grep/Glob exact matching is insufficient. Use for:\n480: - Finding all usages of a pattern by concept/intent\n481: - Locating implementations when exact symbol names are unknown\n482: - Cross-referencing behavior across unfamiliar code paths\n483: \n484: ---\n485: \n486: ## 8. REFERENCES AND RELATED RESOURCES\n487: \n488: The router discovers reference, asset, and script docs dynamically. Start with `references/convergence.md`, `references/loop_protocol.md`, `references/quick_reference.md`, `references/state_format.md`, `assets/deep_review_dashboard.md`, `assets/deep_review_strategy.md`, then load task-specific resources from `references/`, templates from `assets/`, and automation from `scripts/` when present.\n489: \n490: Scripts: `scripts/reduce-state.cjs`, `scripts/runtime-capabilities.cjs`.\n491: \n492: ---\n493: \n494: ## 9. FINDING DEDUP (Packet 110, H-7)\n495: \n496: ### 9.1 Two-Tier Deduplication\n497: \n498: Finding dedup uses a two-tier match at synthesis time:\n499: \n500: 1. **PRIMARY: content_hash** — `sha256(file_path + \"\\u001f\" + line_range + \"\\u001f\" + finding_type + \"\\u001f\" + normalized_description_80chars)`\n501:    - `file_path`: repo-relative path of the finding\n502:    - `line_range`: e.g., `\"42\"` or `\"42-56\"`\n503:    - `finding_type`: one of `security`, `correctness`, `performance`, `maintainability`, `test_quality`, `contract_safety`, `removal`\n504:    - `normalized_description_80chars`: first 80 characters of the finding description, whitespace-collapsed and lowercased\n505: \n506: 2. **FALLBACK (legacy records): file:line + normalized_title**\n507:    - Applied when one or both records lack a `content_hash` field\n508:    - Preserves the existing behavior unchanged\n509: \n510: ### 9.2 Synthesis Behavior\n511: \n512: When the same `content_hash` appears across iterations from different dimensions, the synthesis step collapses them to **ONE entry** with `dimensions: [<list of all dimensions that emitted this finding>]` rather than emitting multiple records.\n513: \n514: Backward compatibility: state records without `content_hash` field fall back to the existing `file:line + normalized_title` behavior. No migration is required for existing JSONL state files.\n515: \n516: ### 9.3 Emission Requirement\n517: \n518: Every finding emitted into the JSONL delta (field `findingDetails[]`) MUST include a `content_hash` field computed per §9.1. The reducer (`reduce-state.cjs`) reads this field for synthesis dedup.\n519: \n520: ---\n521: \n522: ## 10. H-9 DEFERRED\n523: \n524: H-9 (bounded evidence interpolation) is **deferred to packet 111+**. Current deep-review prompts point agents at files and state rather than embedding all evidence inline. When H-9 is implemented, it must name the exact evidence interpolation path and variables to bound before describing candidate file:line windows.\n525: \n526: ---\n527: \n528: Related skills: `deep-research` for investigation loops, `sk-code-review` for single-pass review doctrine, and `system-spec-kit` for command-owned state and continuity saves.\n\n(End of file - total 528 lines)\n</content>","metadata":{"preview":"---\nname: deep-review\ndescription: \"Autonomous iterative code-review loop with externalized state, convergence detection, P0/P1/P2 findings, fresh context per pass.\"\nallowed-tools: [Read, Write, Edit, Bash, Grep, Glob, Task, memory_context, memory_search, mcp__cocoindex_code__search]\n# Note: Task tool is for the command executor (loop management). It combines packet-local candidates, deterministic scoring, repeatable benchmarks, and explicit promotion or rollback gates.\n20: \n21: ---\n22: \n23: ## 1. WHEN TO USE\n24: \n25: ### Activation Triggers\n26: \n27: Use this skill when:\n28: - You want to test whether an agent prompt or instruction surface can be improved\n29: - The mutation boundary is explicit and narrow\n30: - You need packet-local evidence instead of ad hoc prompt tweaking\n31: - You need target-specific benchmark or scoring rules before any canonical mutation\n32: - Promotion must stay gated behind independent evidence plus operator approval\n33: \n34: ### Primary Use Cases\n35: \n36: #### Bounded Agent Improvement\n37: \n38: Use this skill to set up a proposal-first loop for any bounded agent file, write packet-local candidates, and record append-only evidence.\n39: \n40: #### Benchmark-Backed Evaluation\n41: \n42: Use this skill when candidate quality must be judged by produced artifacts and repeatability reports, not just by how a prompt file reads in isolation.\n43: \n44: #### Promotion and Rollback Verification\n45: \n46: Use this skill when you need to prove that guarded promotion, validation, rollback, and post-rollback comparison all work end to end without leaving hidden drift behind.\n47: \n48: ### When NOT to Use\n49: \n50: Do not use this skill for:\n51: - Open-ended prompt rewrites across multiple agent families at once\n52: - Direct canonical edits without a packet-local candidate and evaluator evidence\n53: - Broad runtime-mirror synchronization work presented as benchmark truth\n54: - General packet planning that belongs in `/spec_kit:plan` or implementation that does not need an improvement loop\n55: \n56: ---\n57: \n58: ## 2. SMART ROUTING\n59: \n60: \n61: ### Resource Domains\n62: \n63: The router discovers markdown resources recursively from `references/` and `assets/`, then applies intent scoring so only the guidance that matches the current task is loaded.\n64: \n65: - `references/` for operator workflows, evaluator policy, promotion or rollback rules, target onboarding, and quick-reference guidance\n66: - ### Smart Router Pseudocode\n78: \n79: The authoritative routing logic for scoped markdown loading and explicit runtime-asset loading.\n80: \n81: - Pattern 1: Runtime Discovery - `seen`.\n83: - Pattern 3: Extensible Routing Key - quick-reference, loop, evaluation, promotion, target onboarding, integration, and setup intents route resources.\n84: - Pattern 4: Multi-Tier Graceful Fallback - `UNKNOWN_FALLBACK` asks for target/action/gate disambiguation and missing intent routes return a \"no knowledge base\" notice.\n85: \n86: ```python\n87: from pathlib import evidence path\"]\n127: \n128: def _guard_in_skill(relative_path: str) -> str:\n129:     resolved = (SKILL_ROOT / relative_path).resolve()\n130:     resolved.relative_to(SKILL_ROOT)\n131:     if guarded not in seen:\n169:             load(guarded)\n170:             loaded.append(guarded)\n171:             seen.add(guarded)\n172: \n173:     load_if_available(DEFAULT_RESOURCE)\n174:     for intent in intents:\n175:         for relative_path in RESOURCE_MAP.get(intent, []):\n176:             load_if_available(relative_path)\n177: \n178:     text = _task_text(task)\n179:     if any(keyword in text for keyword in ON_DEMAND_KEYWORDS):\n180:         for paths in RESOURCE_MAP.values():\n181:             for relative_path in paths:\n182:                 load_if_available(relative_path)\n183: \n184:     runtime_assets = list(RUNTIME_ASSETS[\"ALWAYS\"])\n185: \n186:     if not loaded:\n187:         load_if_available(DEFAULT_RESOURCE)\n188:     return {\"intents\": intents, \"resources\": loaded, \"runtime_assets\": runtime_assets}\n189: ```\n190: \n191: ---\n192: \n193: ## 3. HOW IT WORKS\n194: \n195: ### Mode 1: Runtime Initialization\n196: \n197: 1. Confirm the spec folder, target path, execution mode, and active target profile.\n198: 2. Create `{spec_folder}/improvement/` plus the packet-local `candidates/`, `benchmark-runs/`, and `archive/` directories when needed.\n199: 3. Copy in the runtime config, charter, strategy, and boundary templates.\n200: 4. Record baseline state in the append-only ledger before the first candidate run.\n201: \n202: ### Mode 2: Proposal and Evaluation\n203: \n204: 1. Read the charter, boundary file, target profile, and canonical target surface.\n205: 2. Run `scripts/scan-integration.cjs` to discover all surfaces the target agent touches.\n206: 3. Write exactly one bounded candidate under the packet-local `candidates/` directory.\n207: 4. Run `scripts/score-candidate.cjs` to evaluate the candidate via dynamic-mode 5-dimension scoring (the sole supported path).\n208: 5. Run `scripts/run-benchmark.cjs` to measure produced outputs against the active fixture set.\n209: 6. Append score and benchmark results to the packet-local ledger.\n210: 7. Run `scripts/reduce-state.cjs` to refresh the dashboard and experiment registry.\n211: \n212: ### Mode 2A: Stress-Test Failure Paths Before Promotion Claims\n213: \n214: For changes that alter agent discipline, run at least one same-task A/B stress scenario before recommending promotion:\n215: \n216: 1. Call A: a generic improvement attempt against an isolated sandbox copy of the target.\n217: 2. Reset the sandbox to its baseline copy.\n218: 3. Call B: the disciplined `/improve:agent` path against the identical prompt and files.\n219: 4. Judge only grep/file/diff/exit-code signals: helper invocation, packet-local candidate boundary, no canonical or mirror mutation before promotion, benchmark journal boundary, legal-stop gate keys, and stop-reason correctness.\n220: \n221: Do not treat `Read(SKILL.md)` or `skill(deep-agent-improvement)` as evidence that this protocol executed.\n222: \n223: ### 5-Dimension Evaluation Framework\n224: \n225: Dynamic mode is the only scoring path. Scoring evaluates five dimensions:\n226: \n227: | Dimension | Weight | What It Measures |\n228: | --- | --- | --- |\n229: | Structural Integrity | 0.20 | Agent template compliance (required sections present) |\n230: | Rule Coherence | 0.25 | ALWAYS/NEVER rules align with workflow steps |\n231: | Integration Consistency | 0.25 | Mirrors in sync, commands reference agent, skills reference agent |\n232: | Output Quality | 0.15 | Output verification items present, no placeholder content |\n233: | System Fitness | 0.15 | Permission alignment, resource references valid, frontmatter complete |\n234: \n235: Profiles are generated on the fly from any agent file via `scripts/generate-profile.cjs`. No static profiles are shipped; every target is evaluated against its own derived structure and rules.\n236: \n237: ### Mode 3: Promotion and Recovery\n238: \n239: 1. Promote only when prompt scoring, benchmark status, repeatability, boundary, and approval gates all pass.\n240: 2. Use `scripts/promote-candidate.cjs` for guarded canonical mutation.\n241: 3. Use `scripts/rollback-candidate.cjs` plus direct comparison evidence when the canonical target must be restored.\n242: 4. Treat mirror drift as downstream packaging work and review it separately with `scripts/check-mirror-drift.cjs`.\n243: \n244: ---\n245: \n246: ## 4. SUCCESS CRITERIA\n247: \n248: - The loop stays proposal-first unless an explicit guarded promotion path is requested\n249: - Benchmark evidence, prompt scoring, and mirror-sync evidence remain separate\n250: - Reducer outputs make the best-known state, rejected runs, infrastructure failures, and stop conditions easy to review\n251: - Operators can onboard a bounded target without weakening boundary or evaluator guardrails\n252: \n253: ---\n254: \n255: ## 4B. RUNTIME TRUTH CONTRACTS (Phase 005)\n256: \n257: ### Stop-Reason Taxonomy\n258: \n259: Every improvement session termination MUST produce both a `stopReason` (why) and a `sessionOutcome` (what happened).\n260: \n261: **stopReason** (WHY the session ended):\n262: \n263: | Reason | Trigger Condition |\n264: | --- | --- |\n265: | `converged` | All legal-stop gate bundles pass and dimension trajectory is stable |\n266: | `maxIterationsReached` | Iteration counter equals `maxIterations` config |\n267: | `blockedStop` | One or more legal-stop gate bundles fail when convergence math would otherwise trigger stop |\n268: | `manualStop` | Operator cancels the session |\n269: | `error` | Infra failure, script crash, or unrecoverable condition |\n270: | `stuckRecovery` | Session detected stuck state and exhausted recovery options |\n271: \n272: **sessionOutcome** (WHAT happened to the candidate):\n273: \n274: | Outcome | When Used |\n275: | --- | --- |\n276: | `keptBaseline` | Baseline was retained because candidate did not improve |\n277: | `promoted` | Candidate was promoted to canonical target |\n278: | `rolledBack` | Promoted candidate was rolled back to prior state |\n279: | `advisoryOnly` | Session completed for assessment only; no mutation attempted |\n280: \n281: ### Audit Journal Protocol\n282: \n283: All journal emission is orchestrator-only (ADR-001). The journal (`improvement-journal.jsonl`) is an append-only JSONL file capturing lifecycle events. Separate from the existing `agent-improvement-state.jsonl` which tracks proposal/evaluation data.\n284: \n285: **Script**: `scripts/improvement-journal.cjs`\n286: \n287: Event types: `session_start`, `session_initialized`, `integration_scanned`, `candidate_generated`, `candidate_scored`, `benchmark_completed`, `gate_evaluation`, `legal_stop_evaluated`, `blocked_stop`, `promotion_attempt`, `promotion_result`, `rollback`, `rollback_result`, `trade_off_detected`, `mutation_proposed`, `mutation_outcome`, `session_ended`, `session_end`\n288: \n289: ### Static Benchmark Assets\n290: \n291: The reusable benchmark contract ships with the skill, not with each spec packet:\n292: \n293: - Profile: `assets/benchmark-profiles/default.json`\n294: - Fixtures: `assets/benchmark-fixtures/*.json`\n295: - Materializer: `scripts/materialize-benchmark-fixtures.cjs`\n296: - Runner: `scripts/run-benchmark.cjs`\n297: \n298: The command workflow first materializes static fixture JSON into packet-local markdown under `{spec_folder}/improvement/benchmark-outputs/{fixture.id}.md`, then runs `run-benchmark.cjs --profile .opencode/skills/deep-agent-improvement/assets/benchmark-profiles/default.json --outputs-dir {spec_folder}/improvement/benchmark-outputs`. The runner writes `{spec_folder}/improvement/benchmark-outputs/report.json` with `status:\"benchmark-complete\"` and appends a `benchmark_run` row to `{spec_folder}/improvement/agent-improvement-state.jsonl`.\n299: \n300: `benchmark_completed` may be emitted only after `benchmark-outputs/report.json` exists. Repeatability output from `benchmark-stability.cjs` is separate evidence and does not by itself prove benchmark completion.\n301: \n302: ### Legal-Stop Gate Bundles\n303: \n304: A session may NOT claim `converged` unless all five gate bundles pass: `contractGate`, `behaviorGate`, `integrationGate`, `evidenceGate`, and `improvementGate`. The orchestrator emits `legal_stop_evaluated` with nested `details.gateResults` before any `session_end`; failures emit `blocked_stop` with `failedGates[]` and `stopReason:\"blockedStop\"`.\n305: \n306: ### Resume/Continuation Semantics (current release)\n307: \n308: Sessions support a single lineage mode today: `new`. Every invocation of the `/improve:agent` workflow starts a fresh session with a new session id and generation 1. Multi-generation lineage modes (`resume`, `restart`, `fork`, `completed-continue`) were described in earlier drafts but have no shipped runtime wiring in the deep-agent-improvement workflow, reducer, or journal consumer.\n309: \n310: Operators who want to continue evaluating an agent after a prior session SHOULD archive the prior session folder (e.g. move `improve/` to `improve_archive/{timestamp}/`) and re-invoke the command, which starts a new `new`-mode session. The reducer treats each session independently and does not carry ancestry across sessions.\n311: \n312: If the long-form lineage feature is implemented later, it will arrive with first-class event emission in `improve_deep-agent-improvement_{auto,confirm}.yaml`, reducer ancestry handling in `deep-agent-improvement/scripts/reduce-state.cjs`, and replay fixtures. Until then, treat every session as a standalone evaluation.\n313: \n314: ### Mutation Coverage Graph\n315: \n316: **Script**: `scripts/mutation-coverage.cjs`\n317: \n318: Tracks explored dimensions, tried mutation types per dimension, and exhausted mutation sets using `loop_type: \"improvement\"` namespace isolation (ADR-002). The orchestrator skips mutation types already in the exhausted log.\n319: \n320: #### Mutation Signature Dedup (Packet 110, M-3)\n321: \n322: Each mutation entry in `mutation-coverage.json` carries a `signature` field computed as:\n323: \n324: ```\n325: signature = sha256(dimension + \"\\u001f\" + mutationType + \"\\u001f\" + targetSection + \"\\u001f\" + normalizedBody64)\n326: ```\n327: \n328: Where `normalizedBody64` = whitespace-collapsed, lowercased, first 64 characters of the mutation body.\n329: \n330: **Dedup behavior:**\n331: - Before proposing a new mutation, `isSignatureSeen()` scans existing `mutations[]` and `exhausted[]` arrays\n332: - If the signature matches, the candidate is skipped with `reason: \"EXHAUSTED-FROM: iter-NNN\"` recorded in `exhausted[]`\n333: - The `EXHAUSTED-FROM` format references the iteration where the original mutation was tried\n334: \n335: **Bypass:**\n336: ```bash\n337: export DEEP_AGENT_IMPROVEMENT_SKIP_DEDUP=1  # Force re-evaluation of previously seen signatures\n338: ```\n339: When set, `isSignatureSeen()` always returns `{ seen: false }` — every mutation is considered fresh.\n340: \n341: **Backward compatibility:** Legacy `mutation-coverage.json` entries without `signature` field fall back to the existing `dimension::mutationType` dedup in the reducer. No migration required.\n342: \n343: **Authoritative storage:** `mutation-coverage.json` `mutations[]` array — `signature` is written by `recordMutation()` and read by `isSignatureSeen()` and `reduce-state.cjs`.\n344: \n345: ### Dimension Trajectory\n346: \n347: Trajectory data records per-iteration dimension scores. Convergence requires minimum 3 data points (ADR-003) with all dimension deltas within +/-2 across the last 3 points.\n348: \n349: ### Trade-Off Detection\n350: \n351: **Script**: `scripts/trade-off-detector.cjs`\n352: \n353: Detects Pareto trade-offs: flags when improvement > +3 in one dimension causes regression < -3 in hard dimensions (structural, integration, systemFitness) or < -5 in soft dimensions (ruleCoherence, outputQuality). Blocks promotion for Pareto-dominated candidates.\n354: \n355: ### Parallel Candidate Waves (Optional)\n356: \n357: **Script**: `scripts/candidate-lineage.cjs`\n358: \n359: Disabled by default (`parallelWaves.enabled: false` in config, ADR-004). When enabled, spawns 2-3 candidates with different mutation strategies. Activation requires: exploration-breadth score above threshold, 3+ unresolved mutation families, and 2 consecutive tie/plateau iterations.\n360: \n361: ### Weight Optimizer (Advisory Only)\n362: \n363: **Script**: `scripts/benchmark-stability.cjs`\n364: \n365: Reads historical session data and emits a weight-recommendation report. Recommendations do NOT auto-apply (ADR-005). Requires minimum session count threshold before producing recommendations.\n366: \n367: ---\n368: \n369: ## Journal Wiring Contract\n370: \n371: Journal emission is orchestrator-only. The target agent being evaluated never writes journal rows directly; only the visible YAML workflow or an operator-side wrapper invokes `scripts/improvement-journal.cjs`.\n372: \n373: The CLI contract is:\n374: \n375: ```bash\n376: node .opencode/skills/deep-agent-improvement/scripts/improvement-journal.cjs --emit <eventType> --journal <journal_path> --details '<json>'\n377: ```\n378: \n379: The helper validates event type plus `session_end` or `session_ended` details, and the CLI entrypoint stores boundary context under `details`. Top-level `iteration` and `candidateId` fields are available only through the JS API, not through the CLI wrapper used by the YAML workflows.\n380: \n381: ### Boundary Points\n382: \n383: Journal boundaries are `session_start` after baseline setup, per-iteration candidate/scoring/gate events, and `session_end` after synthesis or terminal stop. Required details include session id, target, iteration/candidate paths, scores, stop reason, session outcome, and total iterations.\n384: \n385: ### Frozen Helper Enums\n386: \n387: `improvement-journal.cjs` currently exports and validates the following enums:\n388: \n389: - `STOP_REASONS`: `converged`, `maxIterationsReached`, `blockedStop`, `manualStop`, `error`, `stuckRecovery`\n390: - `SESSION_OUTCOMES`: `keptBaseline`, `promoted`, `rolledBack`, `advisoryOnly`\n391: \n392: Keep session-end emissions aligned to those helper-owned values until the helper contract itself changes. Labels such as `convergedImprovement`, `plateau`, `benchmarkPlateau`, `rejected`, `deferred`, `blocked`, or `errored` are not accepted by the current CLI validator. Plateau detection is a reducer/stop-rule condition; it must reconcile to one of the canonical stop reasons above when emitted as `details.stopReason`.\n393: \n394: ### Orchestrator Ownership\n395: \n396: - Auto mode emits `session_start` after `step_record_baseline`, then emits `candidate_generated`, `candidate_scored`, and `gate_evaluation` inside each loop iteration, and finally emits `session_end` after synthesis.\n397: - Confirm mode mirrors the same boundaries, with `gate_evaluation` emitted after the operator-facing approval gate is resolved.\n398: - Operators invoking the helper manually must use the same boundary order so replay and reducer consumers see a consistent journal shape.\n399: \n400: ### Reducer Consumer Side\n401: \n402: The reducer is the consumer for replay artifacts on refresh. Every `scripts/reduce-state.cjs` pass now attempts to read:\n403: \n404: - `improvement-journal.jsonl`\n405: - `candidate-lineage.json`\n406: - `mutation-coverage.json`\n407: \n408: These inputs remain optional. Missing files do not fail the reducer; the corresponding registry field is set to `null` so dashboard and registry refreshes still complete.\n409: \n410: For legal-stop replay, the reducer consumes `details.gateResults` from the latest `legal_stop_evaluated` event and surfaces it as `journalSummary.latestLegalStop.gateResults` in `experiment-registry.json` plus the dashboard's latest legal-stop table.\n411: \n412: ## ADR-002: Journal Replay Consumer\n413: \n414: ADR-002 is implemented in the reducer via replay consumers instead of a separate orchestrator-only synthesis step. During each refresh pass, `scripts/reduce-state.cjs` now reads the following artifacts when present:\n415: \n416: - `improvement-journal.jsonl` to summarize last session boundaries, total replayed events, per-event counts, and terminal `stopReason` / `sessionOutcome`\n417: - `candidate-lineage.json` to summarize lineage depth, total candidate count, and the latest candidate leaf\n418: - `mutation-coverage.json` to summarize mutation coverage ratio and uncovered mutations\n419: \n420: The reducer writes these summaries into new top-level registry fields:\n421: \n422: - `journalSummary`\n423: - `candidateLineage`\n424: - `mutationCoverage`\n425: \n426: Graceful degradation is required: if any artifact is missing, unreadable, or not yet generated for the current runtime, the reducer preserves the rest of the registry and records `null` for that field instead of throwing.\n427: \n428: The dashboard now also includes a dedicated **Sample Quality** section. This separates replay/stability sample sufficiency from benchmark failures so operators can tell the difference between a true regression and an iteration that simply lacked enough data for trade-off or replay-stability trust.\n429: \n430: ## 5. RULES\n431: \n432: ### ✅ ALWAYS\n433: \n434: - Read the charter, boundary file, and target profile before creating a candidate\n435: - Keep the ledger append-only\n436: - Treat the scorer as independent from the mutator\n437: - Preserve repeatability evidence when benchmark claims are made\n438: - Prefer the simpler candidate when scores tie\n439: - Keep benchmark evidence separate from mirror-drift packaging work\n440: - Require integration evidence to name each expected runtime mirror path explicitly (`.claude/agents`, `.codex/agents`, `.gemini/agents`, plus any declared extra mirrors) before trusting `integrationGate`\n441: \n442: ### ❌ NEVER\n443: \n444: - Mutate the canonical target during proposal-only mode\n445: - Broaden scope beyond the active boundary\n446: - Treat runtime mirrors as experiment truth in the same phase as canonical evaluation\n447: - Treat a stale placeholder mirror path as equivalent to a real runtime mirror\n448: - Hide rejected runs, weak benchmark results, or infra failures\n449: - Promote non-canonical targets even if they benchmark well\n450: \n451: ### ⚠️ ESCALATE IF\n452: \n453: - The target profile and boundary file disagree about mutability or target family\n454: - The benchmark runner cannot produce stable repeatability results\n455: - Promotion evidence is incomplete but canonical mutation is still being requested\n456: - Documentation edits would change the trust boundary rather than clarify it\n457: \n458: ---\n459: \n460: ## 6. REFERENCES\n461: \n462: Core references: `README.md`, `references/quick_reference.md`, `references/loop_protocol.md`, evaluator/promotion/rollback/no-go/onboarding docs, runtime assets under `assets/`, benchmark assets, and helper scripts for scoring, reduction, promotion, rollback, scanning, drift, journal, mutation coverage, trade-offs, candidate lineage, and benchmark stability.\n463: \n464: ---\n465: \n466: ## 7. INTEGRATION POINTS\n467: \n468: - `/improve:agent` initializes and runs the bounded workflow\n469: - `.opencode/agents/deep-agent-improvement.md` provides the mutator surface for deep-agent-improvement runs\n470: - `sk-doc` validators enforce package-shape, README, and markdown document consistency\n471: - `system-spec-kit` packet validation proves phase records remain truthful\n472: \n473: ---\n474: \n475: ## 8. REFERENCES AND RELATED RESOURCES\n476: \n477: The router discovers reference, asset, and script docs dynamically. Start with `references/loop_protocol.md`, `references/quick_reference.md`, `references/benchmark_operator_guide.md`, `references/evaluator_contract.md`, `references/integration_scanning.md`, `references/mirror_drift_policy.md`, `references/no_go_conditions.md`, then load task-specific resources from `references/`, templates from `assets/`, and automation from `scripts/` when present.\n478: \n479: Scripts: `scripts/benchmark-stability.cjs`, `scripts/candidate-lineage.cjs`, `scripts/check-mirror-drift.cjs`, `scripts/generate-profile.cjs`, `scripts/improvement-journal.cjs`, `scripts/materialize-benchmark-fixtures.cjs`, `scripts/mutation-coverage.cjs`, `scripts/promote-candidate.cjs`, `scripts/reduce-state.cjs`, `scripts/rollback-candidate.cjs`, `scripts/run-benchmark.cjs`, `scripts/scan-integration.cjs`, `scripts/score-candidate.cjs`, `scripts/trade-off-detector.cjs`.\n480: \n481: Related skills: `sk-doc` for package-shape and markdown validation, `system-spec-kit` for packet validation, and `sk-prompt` when prompt surfaces need evaluator-backed rewriting.\n\n(End of file - total 481 lines)\n</content>","metadata":{"preview":"---\nname: deep-agent-improvement\ndescription: \"Evaluator-first bounded agent improvement: 5-dim scoring, dynamic profiling, packet-local candidates, guarded promotion.\"\nallowed-tools: [Read, Write, Edit, Bash, Glob, Grep]\nversion: 1.2.2.0\ntriggers:\n  - deep-agent-improvement\n  - agent improvement loop\n  - bounded agent improvement\n  - 5-dimension scoring\n  - integration scanner\n  - dynamic profiling\n---\n\n<!-- Keywords: deep-agent-improvement, deep-agent-improvement, agent-improvement, benchmark-harness, score-candidate, promote-candidate, rollback-candidate -->\n\n# Recursive Agent: Evaluator-First Improvement Orchestrator\n\nEvaluator-first workflow for testing whether a bounded agent surface can be improved without immediately mutating the source of truth. OPERATIONAL MODES — IN-CLI (PRIMARY) + EXTERNAL-CLI (SECONDARY)\n17: \n18: The council is **primarily an IN-CLI capability**. When invoked from inside an active runtime (OpenCode, Claude Code, Codex), the council deliberates using THAT runtime's own models and reasoning lenses as seats. No external dispatch is required for the common case — the active CLI's own model bench (e.g. Opus + Sonnet + Haiku on Claude Code; gpt-5.5 + gpt-5.5-pro + gpt-5.5-xhigh on Codex; opencode-go gateway models on OpenCode) supplies the seat diversity for a round.\n19: \n20: **External-CLI dispatch is a SECONDARY, optional mode** for cases where a different AI vantage adds value (e.g. a fresh Codex perspective from inside a Claude Code session, or DeepSeek/Kimi via cli-opencode from inside a Codex session). It is invoked via the `cli-*` skill family (`cli-claude-code`, `cli-codex`, `cli-opencode`) — never directly from this skill.\n21: \n22: **Both modes obey the one-CLI-per-round invariant** (§4 ALWAYS rule 6):\n23: - In-CLI round: all seats use the current runtime's models.\n24: - External-CLI round: all seats use ONE external CLI (e.g. all `cli-codex` seats with different reasoning levels, OR all `cli-opencode` seats with different gateway models).\n25: - Cross-CLI deliberation is staged as MULTIPLE rounds (one in-CLI + one external, or two different externals) — never folded into the same round.\n26: \n27: The default and most common council run is a single in-CLI round. Add external rounds only when the active runtime cannot supply the required vantage or when explicit cross-AI validation is requested.\n28: \n29: ---\n30: \n31: ## 1. WHEN TO USE\n32: \n33: ### Activation Triggers\n34: \n35: Use this skill when a request needs:\n36: \n37: - Multi-seat AI council deliberation before a plan is chosen.\n38: - Comparison of implementation, refactor, architecture, or research strategies.\n39: - Packet-local persistence of council reports, state, seats, deliberations, and rollback evidence.\n40: - Recovery, audit, or completion checks for existing council artifacts.\n41: \n42: ### Use Cases\n43: \n44: ### Council Planning\n45: \n46: - Compare two or more implementation plans.\n47: - Ask multiple reasoning lenses to critique a proposed direction.\n48: - Decide whether a plan has enough agreement to proceed.\n49: \n50: ### Artifact Persistence\n51: \n52: - Persist a captured council report into packet-local artifacts.\n53: - Verify append-only state records and final `council_complete` events.\n54: - Preserve failed rounds for forensic inspection.\n55: \n56: ### Recovery And Audit\n57: \n58: - Inspect incomplete council output.\n59: - Check convergence decisions against the two-of-three rule.\n60: - Validate planning-only boundaries before handoff to implementation agents.\n61: \n62: ### When NOT to Use\n63: \n64: Do not use this skill for:\n65: \n66: - Direct implementation work, code edits, or spec-doc authorship outside council artifacts.\n67: - Treating council graph rows as source-of-truth or replacing packet-local `ai-council/**` artifacts.\n68: - Single-answer planning where no meaningful strategic disagreement is needed.\n69: - Claims that external AI systems participated when they did not actually run.\n70: \n71: ### Keyword Triggers\n72: \n73: - sk-ai-council\n74: - ai council\n75: - council deliberation\n76: - multi-seat planning\n77: - planning council\n78: - council artifacts\n79: - council convergence\n80: - council graph\n81: - packet-local ai-council\n82: \n83: ---\n84: \n85: ## 2. SMART ROUTING\n86: \n87: ### Primary Detection Signal\n88: \n89: ```bash\n90: request_text=\"$(printf '%s' \"$USER_REQUEST\" | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]')\"\n91: case \"$request_text\" in\n92:   *\"deep ai council\"*|*\"ai council\"*|*\"council deliberation\"*|*\"planning council\"*) COUNCIL_INTENT=1 ;;\n93:   *\"persist council\"*|*\"ai-council artifact\"*|*\"council_complete\"*) COUNCIL_INTENT=1 ;;\n94:   *) COUNCIL_INTENT=0 ;;\n95: esac\n96: ```\n97: \n98: ### Phase Detection\n99: \n100: ```text\n101: TASK CONTEXT\n102:     |\n103:     +- STEP 0: Detect council intent, packet persistence intent, recovery/audit intent, or convergence intent\n104:     +- STEP 1: Score intents and keep top-2 when ambiguity is small\n105:     +- Phase 1: Dispatch or simulate diverse council seats\n106:     +- Phase 2: Deliberate, critique, and test convergence\n107:     +- Phase 3: Persist artifacts, verify state, and hand off planning result\n108: ```\n109: \n110: ### Resource Domains\n111: \n112: The router discovers markdown resources recursively from `references/` and `manual_testing_playbook/`, then applies intent scoring from `INTENT_MODEL`.\n113: \n114: ```text\n115: references/*.md\n116: manual_testing_playbook/**/*.md\n117: ```\n118: \n119: - `references/` contains council state, folder layout, seat diversity, output schema, convergence signals, and caller wiring.\n120: - `manual_testing_playbook/` contains operator validation scenarios for routing, deliberation, persistence, convergence, rollback, scope boundaries, council-graph integration, and council-graph value comparison (32 scenarios across 9 categories).\n121: - `feature_catalog/` mirrors the playbook 1:1 with one user-facing feature entry per scenario (32 entries) — start here for \"what does DAC-NNN actually do\" lookups.\n122: - `scripts/` contains deterministic helpers; scripts are invoked explicitly and are not markdown-routed. Notable entries: `persist-artifacts.cjs` (artifact writer CLI), `replay-graph-from-artifacts.cjs` (DAC-025 derived-projection rebuild — reads `ai-council-state.jsonl` and emits a `council_graph_upsert` payload).\n123: \n124: ### Resource Loading Levels\n125: \n126: | Level | When to Load | Resources |\n127: | --- | --- | --- |\n128: | ALWAYS | Every skill invocation | `references/output_schema.md` |\n129: | CONDITIONAL | Intent signals match | Intent-mapped references from `RESOURCE_MAP` |\n130: | ON_DEMAND | Explicit validation or operator testing | `manual_testing_playbook/manual_testing_playbook.md` and scenario files |\n131: \n132: ### Smart Router Pseudocode\n133: \n134: ```python\n135: from pathlib import Path\n136: \n137: SKILL_ROOT = {doc.relative_to(SKILL_ROOT).as_posix() for doc in docs}\n199: \n200: def classify_intents(user_request, task=None):\n201:     text = \" \".join([str(user_request or \"\"), str(getattr(task, \"intent\", \"\") or \"\")]).lower()\n202:     scores = {intent: 0 for intent in INTENT_MODEL}\n203:     for intent, config in INTENT_MODEL.items():\n204:         for keyword, weight in 0 and (primary_score - secondary_score) <= AMBIGUITY_DELTA:\n213:         return (primary, secondary, scores)\n214:     return (primary, None, scores)\n215: \n216: def get_routing_key(task, intents: route_deep_ai_council_resources(user_request, task=None):\n226:     inventory = discover_markdown_resources()\n227:     primary, secondary, scores = classify_intents(user_request, task)\n228:       \"load_level\": LOAD_LEVELS.get(routing_key, \"CONDITIONAL\"),\n275:         \"resources\": loaded,\n276:     }\n277: ```\n278: \n279: ---\n280: \n281: ## 3. HOW IT WORKS\n282: \n283: ### Council Workflow Overview\n284: \n285: The skill guides planning-only council runs from packet resolution through deliberation, persistence, and handoff. It keeps council artifacts under `ai-council/**` and leaves implementation to the caller or implementation agents.\n286: \n287: **Process Flow**:\n288: \n289: ```text\n290: STEP 1: Resolve And Prepare\n291:        |-- Resolve target spec folder before any persistence\n292:        |-- Load packet context and needed evidence\n293:        |-- Select 2-3 distinct seats\n294:        v\n295: STEP 2: Deliberate And Converge\n296:        |-- Run independent proposals\n297:        |-- Run adversarial cross-seat critique\n298:        |-- Apply two-of-three convergence or emit non-converged status\n299:        v\n300: STEP 3: Persist And Hand Off\n301:        |-- Produce required report sections\n302:        |-- Persist packet-local artifacts when caller has write context\n303:        |-- Verify completion and hand planning to implementation agents\n304: ```\n305: \n306: ### Six-Step Operational Flow\n307: \n308: 1. Resolve the target spec folder before any council execution.\n309: 2. Select two or three distinct council seats with different reasoning lenses and, when real executors are available, different AI vantage targets.\n310: 3. Deliberate across independent proposals, adversarial critique, and convergence reconciliation.\n311: 4. Return a council report with required sections from `references/output_schema.md`.\n312: 5. Persist packet-local artifacts with `scripts/persist-artifacts.cjs` when the caller owns a write-capable context.\n313: 6. Verify completion with `scripts/advise-council-completion.cjs` and the append-only state rules in `references/state_format.md`.\n314: \n315: ### Resource Usage Pattern\n316: \n317: **Scripts**:\n318: \n319: ```bash\n320: node .opencode/skills/sk-ai-council/scripts/persist-artifacts.cjs <packet> --input-file <report>\n321: node .opencode/skills/sk-ai-council/scripts/advise-council-completion.cjs <packet>\n322: ```\n323: \n324: **References**: load `output_schema.md` first, then intent-specific references through Section 2.\n325: \n326: **Manual testing**: load `manual_testing_playbook/manual_testing_playbook.md` only for operator validation and release checks.\n327: \n328: ---\n329: \n330: ## 4. RULES\n331: \n332: ### ✅ ALWAYS\n333: \n334: 1. **ALWAYS keep council writes scoped to packet-local `ai-council/**` artifacts**\n335:    - This preserves the planning-only boundary and avoids mutating implementation or spec-doc surfaces.\n336: \n337: 2. **ALWAYS preserve the planning-only boundary**\n338:    - Implementation remains with implementation agents, commands, or the top-level caller after handoff.\n339: \n340: 3. **ALWAYS use distinct strategy lenses**\n341:    - Label simulated vantages honestly when an external AI system did not actually run.\n342: \n343: 4. **ALWAYS append a `council_complete` event for completed persisted runs**\n344:    - State is append-only and completion must be auditable.\n345: \n346: 5. **ALWAYS treat council graph support as a derived projection**\n347:    - The graph is rebuilt from packet-local `ai-council/**` artifacts and must not replace append-only council state.\n348: \n349: 6. **ALWAYS run a single CLI per round (one-CLI-per-round invariant)**\n350:    - All seats within ONE deliberation round MUST be dispatched through the SAME CLI executor (e.g. all seats from `cli-claude-code`, OR all seats from `cli-opencode`, OR all seats from `cli-codex`). Seat diversity WITHIN a round comes from different models/reasoning lenses on the same CLI (e.g. `opencode-go/deepseek-v4-pro --variant high` + `opencode-go/kimi-k2.6`).\n351:    - Mixing executors within one round (e.g. one seat via Codex + one seat via OpenCode + one seat via Claude Code) is FORBIDDEN — it conflates orchestration boundaries, complicates rollback, and produces noisy convergence signals because per-CLI guarantees (sandbox, runtime, tool surface, output schema) differ.\n352:    - When MULTIPLE CLIs are appropriate for a deliberation, each additional CLI is a NEW DEDICATED ROUND with its own state event, its own seats, and its own convergence pass — never folded into the same round.\n353: \n354: ### ❌ NEVER\n355: \n356: 1. **NEVER write application code, authored spec docs, or files outside `ai-council/**` as part of a council run**\n357:    - The council recommends; it does not implement.\n358: \n359: 2. **NEVER add backward-compatible old-name shims without concrete active-consumer evidence**\n360:    - Rename support should follow real consumers, not speculation.\n361: \n362: 3. **NEVER claim an external CLI or AI system participated unless it actually ran**\n363:    - Simulated perspectives must be explicitly labeled.\n364: \n365: 4. **NEVER rewrite historical state rows**\n366:    - State evolution is additive-only; append new events instead.\n367: \n368: 5. **NEVER mix CLI executors across seats within a single round**\n369:    - See ALWAYS rule 6. A round is defined by its CLI; a CLI change is a round boundary, not a seat boundary.\n370: \n371: ### ⚠️ ESCALATE IF\n372: \n373: 1. **ESCALATE IF no packet/spec folder can be resolved for artifact persistence**\n374:    - Ask for the destination before dispatching seats or writing artifacts.\n375: \n376: 2. **ESCALATE IF required report sections are missing and persistence would be lossy**\n377:    - Fix the report or fail before writes.\n378: \n379: 3. **ESCALATE IF a caller still depends on the old `multi-ai-council` runtime name and cannot be renamed**\n380:    - Compatibility requires explicit user direction.\n381: \n382: 4. **ESCALATE IF a caller asks the council agent itself to mutate graph storage**\n383:    - Graph updates belong to caller-owned `council_graph_*` MCP tooling or reducers, not council-seat deliberation.\n384: \n385: ---\n386: \n387: ## 5. Use `README.md` for human-facing overview and `manual_testing_playbook/manual_testing_playbook.md` for operator validation.\n479: \n480: Related skills: `deep-research` for evidence-first investigation vantages and `system-spec-kit` for packet documentation, validation, resume, and memory continuity.\n\n(End of file - total 480 lines)\n</content>","metadata":{"preview":"---\nname: sk-ai-council\ndescription: \"Deep AI Council: multi-seat planning, artifact persistence, convergence checks, packet-local ai-council outputs.\"\nallowed-tools: [Read, Write, Edit, Bash, Glob, Grep]\nversion: 1.0.0\n---\n\n<!-- Keywords: sk-ai-council, ai council, council deliberation, multi-seat planning, ai-council artifacts, council convergence, planning council, council artifact persistence -->\n\n# Deep AI Council\n\nPlanning-only council deliberation with diverse seats, convergence checks, and packet-local `ai-council/**` artifact persistence.\n\n---\n\n## 0. OPERATIONAL MODES — IN-CLI (PRIMARY) + EXTERNAL-CLI (SECONDARY)\n\nThe council is **primarily an IN-CLI capability**. When invoked from inside an active runtime (OpenCode, Claude Code, Codex), the council deliberates using THAT runtime's own models and reasoning lenses as seats.
