SMART ROUTING\n54: \n55: ### Primary Detection Signal\n56: \n57: Discovery happens through skill-advisor `enhances` edges + trigger phrases, not a dedicated detection script.\n58: \n59: ```text\n60: Operator prompt mentions small-model name or pattern\n61:     |\n62:     +-- Advisor matches trigger phrases (lexical lane)\n63:     +-- cli-devin or cli-opencode already high-confidence\n64:     +-- enhances edge pulls sk-ai-small-model into top-3\n65: ```\n66: \n67: ### Phase Detection\n68: \n69: ```text\n70: TASK CONTEXT\n71:     |\n72:     +- STEP 0: Identify whether a small-model executor is involved\n73:     +- STEP 1: Surface sk-ai-small-model alongside the executor skill\n74:     +- Phase 1: Read references/pattern-index.md\n75:     +- Phase 2: Navigate to the executor-owned pattern file\n76:     +- Phase 3: Apply the pattern from its canonical location\n77: ```\n78: \n79: ### Resource Domains\n80: \n81: ```text\n82: references/\n83:     pattern-index.md      # The only reference; lists owners + ship status\n84: ```\n85: \n86: This skill intentionally has no `assets/` and no `scripts/`. skill.\n126: 2. **Index lookup** — Operator reads `references/pattern-index.md` to find the pattern's canonical location and ship status.\n127: 3. **Navigate to owner** — Operator opens the linked executor file (e.g. `cli-devin/references/context-budget.md`) for the actual pattern body.\n128: 4. **Apply pattern** — Pattern is applied within the executor's prompt-pack or recipe, not from this sentinel.\n129: \n130: ### Dispatch Matrix\n131: \n132: | Model | Executor → Provider (quota pool) | Status |\n133: | --- | --- | --- |\n134: | SWE-1.6 | `cli-devin` → cognition (cognition-free) | (DeepSeek/Kimi/GLM via Devin) — budget defaults, output verification, confidence-scoring rubric, per-model-budgets.json, quota-fallback reference |\n149: | `cli-opencode` | DeepSeek API direct path + `permissions-gate.ts`) |\n152: \n153: ### Adopting a New Provider (Haiku, Gemini Flash, others)\n154: \n155: Metadata-first adoption keeps the sentinel thin:\n156: \n157: 1. Populate the stub in `sk-prompt/assets/model-profiles.json` (set `quota_pool`, `context_length`, etc.).\n158: 2. Optionally set `fallback_target` on existing models that should escalate to the new provider.\n159: 3. Add trigger phrases for the new provider in this skill's `graph-metadata.json` if it has a distinct dispatch shape.\n160: 4. Mark the relevant rows in `references/pattern-index.md` as shipped.\n161: 5. Re-index the advisor (`skill_advisor.py --force-refresh`).\n162: \n163: No code edits are required to adopt a new small-model provider when its quota pool is already represented.\n164: \n165: ---\n166: \n167: ## 4. RULES\n168: \n169: ### ALWAYS\n170: \n171: 1. **Stay thin.** SKILL.md ≤ 200 LOC; pattern-index.md ≤ 100 LOC. If content grows, it belongs in the owning executor skill, not here.\n172: 2. **Link to canonical patterns** — every reference in this skill MUST point at an executor-owned file, never duplicate the pattern body.\n173: 3. **Keep trigger phrases honest.** Add a phrase only when a new model or pattern actually exists. Stale triggers degrade advisor confidence.\n174: 4. **Update the index when downstream phases ship or move files.** The pattern-index is a contract; broken links erode trust.\n175: 5. **Honor the in-scope model set** — SWE-1.6, DeepSeek-v4-pro, Kimi-k2.6, Qwen3.6, GLM-5.1 required; Haiku, Gemini Flash optional. Frontier models (Opus, Sonnet, gpt-5.5) are explicitly out of scope.\n176: \n177: ### NEVER\n178: \n179: 1. **Never add runtime logic here** — no shell commands, no scripts, no agent-config recipes.\n180: 2. **Never duplicate executor patterns** — if a new pattern emerges, ship it in the executor that runs it; only update the index here.\n181: 3. **Never escalate small→frontier** — the user's rotation is small-only. The quota-fallback engine (Phase 005) is pool-aware, not tier-based.\n182: 4. **Never silently drop a stale pattern row.** If a downstream phase deletes a pattern, update the index row to \"deprecated\" with a one-line reason.\n183: \n184: ### ESCALATE IF\n185: \n186: 1. A pattern needs to live in TWO executors (e.g. budget engine in both cli-devin and cli-opencode). Today this is handled via sentinel-style mirror docs (Phase 006). If a true duplicate logic surface emerges, escalate to refactor into a shared asset.\n187: 2. Trigger phrases pull this skill into non-small-model prompts above the 0.5 threshold. Tune weights in `graph-metadata.json` and re-index.\n188: 3. A new small-model provider arrives that does not fit the existing quota-pool model. Update the registry schema in `sk-prompt/assets/model-profiles.json` first, then propagate.\n189: \n190: ---\n191: \n192: ## 5. Ensures proper documentation level selection (1-3+), template usage, and context preservation through AGENTS.md-enforced workflows.\n13: \n14: <!-- ANCHOR:1-when-to-use -->\n15: ## 1. WHEN TO USE\n16: \n17: ### What is a Spec Folder?\n18: \n19: A **spec folder** is a numbered directory (e.g., `007-auth-feature/`) that contains documentation for a single feature/task or a coordinated packet of related phase work:\n20: \n21: Spec folders may also be nested as coordination-root packets with direct-child phase folders (e.g., `specs/02--track/022-feature/011-phase/002-child/`).\n22: \n23: - **Purpose**: Track specifications, plans, tasks, and decisions for one unit of work\n24: - **Location**: Under `specs/` using either `###-short-name/` at the root or nested packet paths for phased coordination\n25: - **Contents**: Markdown files (spec.md, plan.md, tasks.md, and implementation-summary.md when work is complete) plus optional support folders such as `scratch/`, `research/`, or `review/`\n26: \n27: Think of it as a \"project folder\" for AI-assisted development - it keeps context organized and enables session continuity.\n28: \n29: ### Activation Triggers\n30: \n31: **MANDATORY for ALL file modifications:**\n32: - Code files: JS, TS, Python, CSS, HTML\n33: - Documentation: Markdown, README, guides\n34: - Configuration: JSON, YAML, TOML, env templates\n35: - Templates, knowledge base, build/tooling files\n36: \n37: **Request patterns that trigger activation:**\n38: - \"Add/implement/create [feature]\"\n39: - \"Fix/update/refactor [code]\"\n40: - \"Modify/change [configuration]\"\n41: - Any keyword: add, implement, fix, update, create, modify, rename, delete, configure, analyze, phase\n42: \n43: **Example triggers:**\n44: - \"Add email validation to the signup form\" → Level 1-2\n45: - \"Refactor the authentication module\" → Level 2-3\n46: - \"Fix the button alignment bug\" → Level 1\n47: - \"Implement user dashboard with analytics\" → Level 3\n48: \n49: ### When NOT to Use\n50: \n51: - Pure exploration/reading (no file modifications)\n52: - Single typo fixes (<5 characters in one file)\n53: - Whitespace-only changes\n54: - Auto-generated file updates (package-lock.json)\n55: - User explicitly selects Option D (skip documentation)\n56: \n57: **Rule of thumb:** If modifying ANY file content → Activate this skill.\n58: Status: ✅ This requirement applies immediately once file edits are requested.\n59: \n60: ### Distributed Governance Rule\n61: \n62: Any agent writing authored spec folder docs (`spec.md`, `plan.md`, `tasks.md`, `checklist.md`, `implementation-summary.md`, `decision-record.md`, `handover.md`, `review-report.md`, `debug-delegation.md`, `resource-map.md` (optional)) MUST use contract-backed templates through `create.sh` or the inline renderer. This is a workflow-required gate, not a runtime hook: run `bash .opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/scripts/spec/validate.sh <spec-folder> --strict` after authored spec-doc writes and before completion claims, then route continuity updates through /memory:save. Deep-research workflow-owned packet markdown (`research/iterations/*.md`, `research/deep-research-*.md`, and progressive `research/research.md` loop updates) is exempt from that generic per-write rule; `/spec_kit:deep-research` must instead run targeted strict validation after every `spec.md` mutation it performs. @deep-research retains exclusive write access for `research/research.md`; @debug retains exclusive write access for `debug-delegation.md`.\n63: \n64: - `handover.md` stays in the canonical recovery ladder and is maintained through `/memory:save` handover_state routing using the handover template for initial creation.\n65: - `review-report.md` remains owned by `@deep-review` when deep review workflows synthesize findings.\n66: - `resource-map.md` is a peer cross-cutting template under `.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/templates/`; it remains optional at any level and gives reviewers a lean file ledger alongside `implementation-summary.md`.\n67: \n68: ### Utility Template Triggers\n69: \n70: | Template              | Trigger Keywords                                                                                                              | Action                    |\n71: | --------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------- |\n72: | `handover.md`         | \"handover\", \"next session\", \"continue later\", \"pass context\", \"ending session\", \"save state\", \"multi-session\", \"for next AI\"  | Suggest `/memory:save` handover maintenance |\n73: | `debug-delegation.md` | \"stuck\", \"can't fix\", \"tried everything\", \"same error\", \"fresh eyes\", \"hours on this\", \"still failing\", \"need help debugging\" | Suggest Task-tool debug delegation |\n74: \n75: **Rule:** When detected, proactively suggest the appropriate action.\n76: \n77: <!-- /ANCHOR:1-when-to-use -->\n78: \n79: ---\n80: \n81: <!-- ANCHOR:2-smart-routing -->\n82: ## 2. SMART ROUTING\n83: \n84: ### Resource Domains\n85: \n86: The router discovers markdown resources recursively from `references/` and `assets/` and then applies intent scoring from `RESOURCE_MAP`. Keep this section domain-focused rather than static file inventories.\n87: \n88: - `references/memory/` for context retrieval, save workflows, trigger behavior, and indexing.\n89: - `references/templates/` for level selection, template selection, and structure guides.\n90: - `references/validation/` for checklist policy, verification rules, decision formats, and template compliance contracts.\n91: - `references/structure/` for folder organization and sub-folder versioning.\n92: - `references/workflows/` for command workflows and worked examples.\n93: - `references/debugging/` for troubleshooting and root-cause methodology.\n94: - `references/config/` for runtime environment configuration.\n95: \n96: ### Template and Script Sources of Truth\n97: \n98: - Level definitions and template size guidance: level specifications reference\n99: - Template usage and composition rules: [template_guide.md](./references/templates/template_guide.md)\n100: - Use the Level contract for operational templates; `create.sh` and the Level contract resolver share the same template index.\n\n(Showing lines 1-100 of 489. Each cli-* SKILL.md provides its own provider-specific dictionaries (`INTENT_SIGNALS`, `RESOURCE_MAP`, `LOADING_LEVELS`, `UNKNOWN_FALLBACK_CHECKLIST`) inline; this reference holds the shared procedural code.\n9: \n10: > Pattern: see [sk-doc smart-router resilience template](../../sk-doc/assets/skill/skill_smart_router.md).\n11: \n12: ---\n13: \n14: ## 1. OVERVIEW\n15: \n16: Canonical helper-function bodies (_task_text, _guard_in_skill, discover_markdown_resources, score_intents, select_intents, route_<provider>_resources) shared across the five cli-* sibling skills. Each cli-* skill provides its own INTENT_SIGNALS, RESOURCE_MAP, LOADING_LEVELS, UNKNOWN_FALLBACK_CHECKLIST inline.\n17: \n18: ---\n19: \n20: ## 2. HELPER FUNCTIONS\n21: \n22: ```python\n23: from pathlib import Path\n24: \n25: SKILL_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parent\n26: RESOURCE_BASES = (SKILL_ROOT / \"references\", SKILL_ROOT / \"assets\")\n27: DEFAULT_RESOURCE = \"references/cli_reference.md\"\n28: \n29: def _task_text(task) -> str:\n30:     return \" \".join([\n31:         str(getattr(task, \"text\", \"\")),\n32:         str(getattr(task, \"query\", \"\")),\n33:         \" \".join(getattr(task, \"keywords\", []) or []),\n34:     ]).lower()\n35: \n36: def _guard_in_skill(relative_path: str) -> str:\n37:     resolved = (SKILL_ROOT / relative_path).resolve()\n38:     resolved.relative_to(SKILL_ROOT)\n39:     if resolved.suffix.lower() != \".md\":\n40:         raise ValueError(f\"Only markdown resources are routable: {relative_path}\")\n41:     return resolved.relative_to(SKILL_ROOT).as_posix()\n42: \n43: def discover_markdown_resources() -> set[str]:\n44:     docs = []\n45:     for base in RESOURCE_BASES:\n46:         if base.exists():\n47:             docs.extend(p for p in base.rglob(\"*.md\") if p.is_file())\n48:     return {doc.relative_to(SKILL_ROOT).as_posix() for doc in docs}\n49: \n50: def score_intents(task) -> dict[str, float]:\n51:     text = _task_text(task)\n52:     scores = {intent: 0.0 for intent in INTENT_SIGNALS}\n53:     for intent, cfg in INTENT_SIGNALS.items():\n54:         for keyword in cfg[\"keywords\"]:\n55:             if keyword in text:\n56:                 scores[intent] += cfg[\"weight\"]\n57:     return scores\n58: \n59: def select_intents(scores: dict[str, float], ambiguity_delta: float = 1.0, max_intents: int = 2) -> list[str]:\n60:     ranked = sorted(scores.items(), key=lambda item: item[1], reverse=True)\n61:     if not ranked or ranked[0][1] <= 0:\n62:         return [\"UNKNOWN\"]\n63:     selected = [ranked[0][0]]\n64:     if len(ranked) > 1 and ranked[1][1] > 0 and (ranked[0][1] - ranked[1][1]) <= ambiguity_delta:\n65:         selected.append(ranked[1][0])\n66:     return selected[:max_intents]\n67: \n68: def get_routing_key(task, intents: list[str]) -> str:\n69:     explicit = str(getattr(task, \"provider\", \"\")).strip().lower()\n70:     if explicit:\n71:         return explicit\n72:     return \"<PROVIDER>\" if intents else \"unknown\"\n73: \n74: def route_<PROVIDER>_resources(task):\n75:     inventory = discover_markdown_resources()\n76:     scores = score_intents(task)\n77:     intents = select_intents(scores, ambiguity_delta=1.0)\n78:     routing_key = get_routing_key(task, intents)\n79:     loaded = []\n80:     seen = set()\n81: \n82:     def load_if_available(relative_path: str) -> None:\n83:         guarded = _guard_in_skill(relative_path)\n84:         if guarded in inventory and guarded not in seen:\n85:             load(guarded)\n86:             loaded.append(guarded)\n87:             seen.add(guarded)\n88: \n89:     # 1. ALWAYS load baseline + fast-path prompt-quality asset\n90:     for relative_path in LOADING_LEVELS[\"ALWAYS\"]:\n91:         load_if_available(relative_path)\n92: \n93:     # 2. UNKNOWN FALLBACK: no keywords matched at all\n94:     if max(scores.values()) == 0:\n95:         return {\n96:             \"intents\": [\"UNKNOWN\"],\n97:             \"routing_key\": routing_key,\n98:             \"load_level\": \"UNKNOWN_FALLBACK\",\n99:             \"needs_disambiguation\": True,\n100:             \"disambiguation_checklist\": UNKNOWN_FALLBACK_CHECKLIST,\n101:             \"resources\": loaded,\n102:         }\n103: \n104:     # 3. CONDITIONAL: intent-mapped resources\n105:     for intent in intents:\n106:         for relative_path in RESOURCE_MAP.get(intent, []):\n107:             load_if_available(relative_path)\n108: \n109:     # 4. ON_DEMAND: explicit keyword triggers\n110:     text = _task_text(task)\n111:     if any(keyword in text for keyword in LOADING_LEVELS[\"ON_DEMAND_KEYWORDS\"]):\n112:         for relative_path in LOADING_LEVELS[\"ON_DEMAND\"]:\n113:             load_if_available(relative_path)\n114: \n115:     # 5. Safety net\n116:     if not loaded:\n117:         load_if_available(DEFAULT_RESOURCE)\n118: \n119:     result = {\"intents\": intents, \"routing_key\": routing_key, \"intent_scores\": scores, \"resources\": loaded}\n120:     if len(loaded) <= len(LOADING_LEVELS[\"ALWAYS\"]):\n121:         result[\"notice\"] = f\"No knowledge base found for routing key '{routing_key}' beyond always-load resources\"\n122:     return result\n123: ```\n124: \n125: Replace `<PROVIDER>` with the provider slug (`claude_code`, `codex`, `devin`, `gemini`, `opencode`).\n126: \n127: ---\n128: \n129: ## 3. LOADING-LEVEL SEMANTICS\n130: \n131: | Level         | When to load            | Resources                                                       |\n132: | ------------- | ----------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------- |\n133: | `ALWAYS`      | Every skill invocation  | `references/cli_reference.md`, `assets/prompt_quality_card.md`  |\n134: | `CONDITIONAL` | If intent signals match | Intent-mapped reference docs from `RESOURCE_MAP`                |\n135: | `ON_DEMAND`   | Only on explicit request| Extended templates and patterns (gated by `ON_DEMAND_KEYWORDS`) |\n136: \n137: ---\n138: \n139: ## 4. UNKNOWN_FALLBACK RETURN CONTRACT\n140: \n141: When no keyword matches `score_intents()` returns all-zero scores. The router returns:\n142: \n143: ```python\n144: {\n145:     \"intents\": [\"UNKNOWN\"],\n146:     \"load_level\": \"UNKNOWN_FALLBACK\",\n147:     \"needs_disambiguation\": True,\n148:     \"disambiguation_checklist\": UNKNOWN_FALLBACK_CHECKLIST,\n149:     \"resources\": loaded,  # ALWAYS-tier resources only\n150: }\n151: ```\n152: \n153: The caller surfaces `disambiguation_checklist` to the user before re-routing.\n154: \n155: ---\n156: \n157: ## 5. PROVIDER-SPECIFIC DICTIONARIES\n158: \n159: Each cli-* SKILL.md provides its own:\n160: - `INTENT_SIGNALS` — provider-specific keyword-to-weight intent map\n161: - `RESOURCE_MAP` — provider-specific intent-to-reference-files map\n162: - `LOADING_LEVELS` — provider-specific `ALWAYS` / `ON_DEMAND_KEYWORDS` / `ON_DEMAND` lists\n163: - `UNKNOWN_FALLBACK_CHECKLIST` — provider-specific disambiguation prompts\n164: \n165: See the per-skill SKILL.md §2 Smart Routing for these inline dictionaries.\n166: \n167: ---\n\n(End of file - total 167 lines)\n</content>","metadata":{"preview":"---\ntitle: Shared Smart-Router Helpers for cli-* Skills\ndescription: Canonical helper-function bodies (_task_text, _guard_in_skill, discover_markdown_resources, score_intents, select_intents, route_<provider>_resources) shared across the five cli-* sibling skills. OVERVIEW\n13: \n14: Canonical 7-step Memory Handback procedure shared across the five cli-* sibling skills. Covers MEMORY_HANDBACK extraction, structured-JSON normalization, generate-context.js dispatch modes, and the post-010 save gates.\n15: \n16: ---\n17: \n18: ## 2. PROCEDURE (7 STEPS)\n19: \n20: 1. **Include epilogue**: Append the Spec-Doc Record Epilogue template (see the cli-* skill's `assets/prompt_templates.md` §N — the section number is cited inline in the skill's §4) to the delegated prompt.\n21: 2. **Extract section**: After receiving agent output, extract the `MEMORY_HANDBACK` section using: `/<!-- MEMORY_HANDBACK_START -->([\\s\\S]*?)<!-- MEMORY_HANDBACK_END -->/`\n22: 3. **Convert to structured JSON**: Build the JSON-primary payload that `generate-context.js` documents. Use `specFolder`, `user_prompts`, `observations`, and `recent_context` as the canonical field names in new examples. Add `FILES`, `sessionSummary`, `keyDecisions`, `nextSteps`, `triggerPhrases`, `toolCalls`, `exchanges`, `preflight`, and `postflight` when the delegated run produced that evidence.\n23: 4. **Redact and scrub**: Remove secrets, tokens, credentials, and any unnecessary sensitive values before writing the JSON file or sending the payload to the save script.\n24: 5. **Choose a structured-input mode**: Save the scrubbed payload to `/tmp/save-context-data-<session-id>.json`, pipe it with `--stdin`, or pass it inline with `--json`.\n25: 6. **Invoke generate-context.js**: Use one of:\n26:    - `node .opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/scripts/dist/memory/generate-context.js /tmp/save-context-data-<session-id>.json [spec-folder]`\n27:    - `printf '%s' \"$JSON_PAYLOAD\" | node .opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/scripts/dist/memory/generate-context.js --stdin [spec-folder]`\n28:    - `node .opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/scripts/dist/memory/generate-context.js --json \"$JSON_PAYLOAD\" [spec-folder]`\n29: 7. **Index**: Run `memory_index_scan({ specFolder })` for immediate MCP visibility.\n30: \n31: ---\n32: \n33: ## 3. CAVEATS\n34: \n35: **Delimiter missing**: If agent output lacks `MEMORY_HANDBACK` delimiters, the calling AI manually constructs the structured JSON payload and saves it through the same JSON-primary path. The save flow normalizes `nextSteps` or `next_steps`; the first entry persists as `Next: ...` and drives `NEXT_ACTION`, and remaining entries persist as `Follow-up: ...`.\n36: \n37: **Structured JSON only**: Direct spec-folder-only invocation is no longer supported. Always call `generate-context.js` with `--stdin`, `--json`, or a JSON temp file.\n38: \n39: **Explicit target precedence**: If you pass `[spec-folder]` on the CLI, that explicit target wins over any `specFolder` value inside the payload.\n40: \n41: **Explicit JSON mode failures**: If the explicit data file cannot be loaded, `generate-context.js` fails with `EXPLICIT_DATA_FILE_LOAD_FAILED: ...`. Do not fall back to OpenCode capture in that case; surface the error and stop.\n42: \n43: **Post-010 save gates**: Valid JSON can still be rejected after normalization. File-backed handbacks skip the stateless alignment and `QUALITY_GATE_ABORT` checks, but they still fail with `INSUFFICIENT_CONTEXT_ABORT` when the payload is too thin and with `CONTAMINATION_GATE_ABORT` when it includes content from another spec.\n44: \n45: **Compatibility aliases**: The normalizer still accepts documented camelCase and snake_case pairs such as `sessionSummary` / `session_summary`, `nextSteps` / `next_steps`, `userPrompts` / `user_prompts`, and `recentContext` / `recent_context`. Prefer the canonical field names shown above in new handback payloads.\n46: \n47: **Minimum payload guidance**: Include a specific `sessionSummary`, at least one meaningful `recent_context` entry or equivalent observation, and rich `FILES` entries with a descriptive `DESCRIPTION`. Add `ACTION`, `MODIFICATION_MAGNITUDE`, and `_provenance` when known so the saved memory carries durable evidence instead of bare filenames.\n48: \n49: ---\n50: \n51: ## 4. The audit-trail schema is additive v1.1 → v1.2 with new `artifact_written` and `rollback` event types; v1 readers continue to parse v1.2 files unchanged. Round-NNN folder is the rollback unit; on seat error or convergence failure, the round artifacts move to `failed/round-NNN-<timestamp>/` and the audit trail records `superseded_by: \"rollback\"` markers. Three ADRs (write-permission model, audit-trail schema, rollback semantics) document the decisions. 7 new vitest cases cover permission-scope, runtime-parity, audit-trail, and rollback.\n\n\n/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skills/cli-gemini/SKILL.md:\n  Line 251: | Multi-strategy planning | `@multi-ai-council` | `gemini \"As @multi-ai-council agent: Plan the authentication redesign\" -m gemini-3.1-pro-preview -o text` |\n\n\n/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skills/cli-codex/SKILL.md:\n  Line 282: | Multi-strategy planning | multi-ai-council | `codex exec -p multi-ai-council \"Plan the authentication redesign\" -m gpt-5.5` |\n\n\n/Users/michelkerkmeester/MEGA/Development/Code_Environment/Public/.opencode/skills/cli-claude-code/SKILL.md:\n  Line 32: - AI agents executing these scenarios must run the actual `opencode run` invocations, inspect real outputs, capture real exit codes and verify real behavior. The only acceptable classifications are PASS, FAIL or SKIP (with a specific sandbox blocker documented). \"UNAUTOMATABLE\" is not a valid status.\n9: \n10: > **SELF-INVOCATION GUARD**: The cli-opencode skill is the only cli-* skill that targets the same binary that runs OpenCode itself. Use cases 1 and 3 must be invoked from a non-OpenCode runtime (Claude Code, Codex, Copilot, Gemini, raw shell). Use case 2 (parallel detached session) is the documented exception that lets an in-OpenCode operator spawn a SEPARATE session via `--share --port <N>` with explicit parallel-session keywords. OVERVIEW\n55: \n56: This playbook provides 34 deterministic scenarios across 9 categories validating the `cli-opencode` skill surface. Each feature keeps its global `CO-NNN` ID and links to a dedicated feature file with the full execution contract.\n57: \n58: Coverage note (2026-04-26): Covers the canonical default invocation (`opencode-go/deepseek-v4-pro` + `--variant high` + `--agent general` + `--format json`), the three documented use cases (external dispatch, parallel detached, cross-AI handback per ADR-002), the multi-provider matrix (opencode-go default with full variant range, deepseek direct API), the 8-agent routing surface (general / context / orchestrate / write / review / debug / deep-research / deep-review / multi-ai-council), session continuity surfaces (`-c`, `-s <id>`, `--fork`, `--share` gate), the 13-template inventory plus CLEAR quality card, the parallel-detached exception path with `</dev/null` worker farms, cross-repo dispatch via `--dir` and cross-server dispatch via `--attach`. Self-invocation refusal (ADR-001) is enforced upstream by the skill's layered detection guard and is exercised in CO-008 (refusal path) and CO-031 (cross-repo nested guard) respectively. Destructive scenarios are limited to operator-confirmed `--share` flows (CHK-033). The playbook never publishes share URLs without explicit operator approval.\n59: \n60: ### Realistic Test Model\n61: \n62: 1. A realistic user request is given to an orchestrator running on a non-OpenCode runtime (Claude Code, Codex, Copilot, Gemini or raw shell), OR an in-OpenCode operator with explicit parallel-session keywords.\n63: 2. The orchestrator decides whether to delegate to OpenCode CLI via cli-opencode, picks the right model + agent + variant + format + dir and constructs a Role -> Context -> Action -> Format prompt per the prompt quality card.\n64: 3. The operator captures both the dispatch command and the user-visible outcome (JSON event stream parsed, tool.calls surfaced, session.completed summary).\n65: 4. The scenario passes only when the dispatch is sound, the OpenCode output matches the expected signals and the returned result would satisfy a real user.\n66: \n67: ### What Each Feature File Should Explain\n68: \n69: - The realistic user request that should trigger the delegation\n70: - The orchestrator brief or OpenCode-facing prompt that should drive the test\n71: - The expected execution process, including model + agent + variant + format + dir choices and any session-management decisions\n72: - The desired user-visible outcome\n73: - The implementation or skill-doc anchors that justify the scenario\n74: \n75: ---\n76: \n77: ## 2. GLOBAL PRECONDITIONS\n78: \n79: 1. Working directory is project root and contains `.git/`.\n80: 2. OpenCode CLI is installed and on PATH: `command -v opencode` returns a non-empty path. If absent, install via `brew install opencode` (macOS) or `curl -fsSL https://opencode.ai/install | bash`.\n81: 3. OpenCode CLI version is at or near the v1.3.17 baseline pinned in `references/cli_reference.md`. Drift handled per `references/cli_reference.md` §9.\n82: 4. The GitHub Copilot subscription is active and registered in `opencode auth list` (the canonical default `opencode-go/deepseek-v4-pro` resolves through it). The `opencode-go/deepseek-v4-pro` Anthropic alternative also resolves through the same OAuth (no separate Anthropic credentials required). Multi-provider scenarios additionally need: opencode-go subscription registered when exercising `opencode-go/deepseek-v4-pro` and direct DeepSeek API credentials (`DEEPSEEK_API_KEY` / `auth login deepseek`) when exercising `deepseek/...`.\n83: 5. The active runtime for use case 1 and 3 scenarios is NOT OpenCode itself. Confirm by checking no `OPENCODE_*` env vars are set: `env | grep -q '^OPENCODE_' && echo IN-OPENCODE || echo OK`. Use case 2 scenarios (CO-026, CO-027, CO-028) explicitly include the parallel-session keywords required to permit the dispatch from inside OpenCode.\n84: 6. The skill's reference and asset files exist at `.opencode/skills/cli-opencode/{references,assets}/` so prompt-quality, template and routing scenarios resolve.\n85: 7. The project's MCP servers (Spec Kit Memory, CocoIndex Code) are registered in `opencode.json` so use case 1 (CO-006) and use case 3 (CO-021, CO-022) scenarios can call `memory_health`, CocoIndex search and `memory_search`.\n86: 8. The operator's repo root resolves via `REPO_ROOT=\"$(pwd)\"` (run from the project root). Most scenarios pass `--dir \"$(pwd)\"` directly so they portably target whichever repo the operator runs them in. The `<repo-root>` placeholders in prose refer to the same value. Adapt to a different absolute path only if a scenario explicitly requires a non-default repo (e.g., CO-029 cross-repo dispatch derives a sibling path via `dirname \"$(pwd)\"`).\n87: 9. Destructive scenarios involving `--share` (CO-026, CO-027, CO-028) MUST follow strict sandboxing and recovery rules. Each MUST run with `--dir /tmp/co-share-sandbox-NNN/` (where NNN is the scenario ID). Each MUST NOT run with `--dir` pointing at the operator project tree. Each MUST NOT publish the share URL to anyone without explicit operator confirmation per CHK-033. Recovery is mandatory after every run (pass or fail). Step (a) revoke every captured share URL via `opencode session revoke ${SESSION_ID}`. Step (b) remove the sandbox tmpdir via `rm -rf /tmp/co-share-sandbox-NNN/`. The test only validates the session-creation path. No real URL publication occurs.\n88: \n89: ---\n90: \n91: ## 3. GLOBAL EVIDENCE REQUIREMENTS\n92: \n93: - Full command transcript including the exact `opencode run` invocation with all flags\n94: - The user request that triggered the delegation\n95: - The orchestrator-side reasoning for model + agent + variant + format + dir selection\n96: - The Role -> Context -> Action -> Format prompt actually dispatched (not just paraphrased)\n97: - OpenCode JSON event stream captured to file (`.jsonl`)\n98: - Exit code from `opencode run`\n99: - Session id captured from the `session.started` event\n100: - The session.completed payload summary\n\n(Showing lines 1-100 of 879. OVERVIEW\n55: \n56: This playbook provides 27 deterministic scenarios across 9 categories validating the `cli-devin` skill surface. Each feature keeps its global `DV-NNN` ID and links to a dedicated feature file with the full execution contract. v1.0.2.0: wave-2 run promoted 8 SKIPs to PASS, split DV-018 into shell-runnable (new DV-027 cloud surface) + manual round-trip (DV-018), and reaffirmed 3 calling-AI orchestrator-layer SKIPs (DV-017 / DV-019 / DV-020).\n57: \n58: Coverage note (2026-05-15): Covers the canonical default invocation (`swe-1.6` + `--permission-mode auto`), every documented permission mode, every model preset (SWE-1.6 default + DeepSeek v4 primary for complex + GLM 5.1 and Kimi k2.6 as complex-task fallbacks), every Devin-side surface (`devin rules`, `devin skills`, `devin mcp`), session continuity (`--continue`, `--resume <id>`, `devin list`), the Devin-unique local-to-cloud handoff with the 5-check operator-confirmation gate, the layered self-invocation guard, cross-AI dispatch from each of the four sibling cli-* runtimes, and the `devin acp` Agent Client Protocol server.\n59: \n60: ### Realistic Test Model\n61: \n62: 1. A realistic user request is given to an orchestrator running on a non-Devin runtime (Claude Code, Codex, Gemini, OpenCode or shell).\n63: 2. The orchestrator decides whether to delegate to Devin via the `cli-devin` skill, picks the right model preset and permission mode, and uses the canonical prompt for the scenario: natural-human by default, RCAF only when the actor is an AI orchestrator.\n64: 3. The operator captures both the dispatch command and the user-visible outcome.\n65: 4. The scenario passes only when the dispatch is sound, the Devin output matches the expected signals and the returned result would satisfy a real user.\n66: \n67: ### What Each Feature File Should Explain\n68: \n69: - The realistic user request that should trigger the delegation\n70: - The orchestrator brief or Devin-facing prompt that should drive the test\n71: - The expected execution process, including model preset, permission mode and any session-management decisions\n72: - The desired user-visible outcome\n73: - The implementation or skill-doc anchors that justify the scenario\n74: \n75: ---\n76: \n77: ## 2. GLOBAL PRECONDITIONS\n78: \n79: 1. Working directory is project root and contains `.git/`.\n80: 2. Devin CLI is installed and on PATH: `command -v devin` returns a non-empty path. If not installed, run `curl -fsSL https://cli.devin.ai/install.sh | bash` (macOS/Linux) or `irm https://static.devin.ai/cli/setup.ps1 | iex` (Windows).\n81: 3. Devin CLI is authenticated: `devin auth status` returns an authenticated state. If not, run `devin auth login` and paste a token from `https://app.devin.ai` (Cognition / Codeium / Windsurf bridge) (or use `devin setup` for the interactive wizard).\n82: 4. The active runtime is NOT Devin itself — the self-invocation guard in SKILL.md §2 must not trip. Verify by running `env | grep -i '^DEVIN_'` and confirming no `DEVIN_*` vars are set.\n83: 5. The skill's reference and asset files exist at `.opencode/skills/cli-devin/{references,assets}/` so prompt-quality and template scenarios resolve.\n84: 6. Documented model presets are `swe-1.6` (default), `deepseek-v4` (primary for complex tasks), `glm-5.1` (complex-task fallback — agentic / tool-use), and `kimi-k2.6` (complex-task fallback — large context). Do not substitute alternative model IDs.\n85: 7. `--permission-mode auto` is the documented skill default. Escalation to `dangerous` requires explicit operator approval recorded in the scenario evidence.\n86: 8. Destructive scenario `DV-007` (`--permission-mode dangerous` + `--sandbox`) MUST run only against rebuildable, non-production data and requires explicit human approval before execution.\n87: 9. Cloud-handoff scenarios `DV-018` and `DV-020` require a Devin account provisioned for cloud sessions. Operators without that entitlement may SKIP these scenarios with a documented blocker.\n88: \n89: ---\n90: \n91: ## 3. GLOBAL EVIDENCE REQUIREMENTS\n92: \n93: - Full command transcript including the exact `devin` invocation with all flags\n94: - The user request that triggered the delegation\n95: - The orchestrator-side reasoning for model preset and permission-mode selection\n96: - The canonical prompt actually dispatched (not just paraphrased), whether natural-human or RCAF for AI-orchestrator scenarios\n97: - Devin stdout (and stderr captured via `2>&1`)\n98: - Exit code from the `devin` invocation\n99: - The final user-facing outcome and a PASS, PARTIAL or FAIL verdict with rationale\n100: \n101: ---\n102: \n103: ## 4. DETERMINISTIC COMMAND NOTATION\n104: \n105: - CLI commands shown as `devin <subcommand> [args]` (e.g. `devin --prompt-file /tmp/p.md --model swe-1.6 --permission-mode auto`)\n106: - Bash commands shown as `bash: <command>` (e.g. `bash: command -v devin`)\n107: - File capture shown as `> /tmp/<file>` (orchestrator captures Devin output to a temp file for inspection)\n108: - `->` separates sequential steps in the command sequence column\n109: - Always append `2>&1 </dev/null` for non-interactive / background dispatches per the family stdin-redirect convention\n110: \n111: ---\n112: \n113: ## 5. REVIEW PROTOCOL AND RELEASE READINESS\n114: \n115: ### Inputs Required\n116: \n117: 1. `manual_testing_playbook.md`\n118: 2. Referenced per-feature files under `manual_testing_playbook/NN--category-name/`\n119: 3. Scenario execution evidence (transcripts, captured stdout files, exit codes)\n120: 4. Feature-to-scenario coverage map\n121: 5. Triage notes for all non-pass outcomes\n122: \n123: ### Scenario Acceptance Rules\n124: \n125: For each executed scenario, check:\n126: \n127: 1. Preconditions were satisfied (Devin installed, authenticated, non-Devin runtime).\n128: 2. Prompt and command sequence were executed as written, including `--permission-mode <mode>` and `2>&1 </dev/null` where applicable.\n129: 3. Expected signals are present in Devin stdout / stderr / exit code.\n130: 4. Evidence is complete and readable.\n131: 5. Outcome rationale is explicit.\n132: \n133: Scenario verdict:\n134: - `PASS`: all acceptance checks true\n135: - `PARTIAL`: core behavior works but non-critical evidence (e.g. timing data) is incomplete\n136: - `FAIL`: expected behavior missing, contradictory output, dispatch broken or critical check failed\n137: - `SKIP`: documented blocker (e.g. no cloud entitlement for DV-018) — count toward coverage with explicit rationale\n138: \n139: ### Feature Verdict Rules\n140: \n141: - `PASS`: all mapped scenarios for feature are `PASS`\n142: - `PARTIAL`: at least one mapped scenario is `PARTIAL`, none are `FAIL`\n143: - `FAIL`: any mapped scenario is `FAIL`\n144: \n145: Hard rule:\n146: - Any critical-path scenario `FAIL` (DV-001, DV-005, DV-019) forces feature verdict to `FAIL`. The default invocation, default permission mode and self-invocation guard are the load-bearing baseline. If any of them fail the skill cannot be released.\n147: \n148: ### Release Readiness Rule\n149: \n150: Release is `READY` only when:\n151: \n152: 1. No feature verdict is `FAIL`.\n153: 2. All critical scenarios (`DV-001`, `DV-005`, `DV-019`) are `PASS`.\n154: 3. Coverage is 100% of playbook scenarios defined by the root index and backed by per-feature files (`COVERED_FEATURES == TOTAL_FEATURES`, currently 25). SKIPs with documented blockers count toward coverage.\n155: 4. No unresolved blocking triage item remains.\n156: \n157: ### Root-vs-Feature Rule\n158: \n159: Keep global verdict logic in the root playbook. Put feature-specific acceptance caveats (e.g. bypass-mode approval evidence for DV-007, cloud entitlement for DV-018) in the matching per-feature files.\n160: \n161: ### Destructive Scenarios\n162: \n163: - `DV-007` (`--permission-mode dangerous`): MUST run with explicit user approval and against a sandbox folder, not the live workspace. Capture the approval acknowledgement as evidence.\n164: - `DV-018` (cloud handoff round-trip): transmits local repo state to Cognition's cloud sandbox. MUST complete the 5-check gate from `references/cloud_handoff.md` §3 before dispatch.\n165: \n166: ---\n167: \n168: ## 6. SUB-AGENT ORCHESTRATION AND WAVE PLANNING\n169: \n170: ### Purpose\n171: \n172: This section records wave planning and capacity guidance for the manual testing package. It is not a runtime support matrix by itself.\n173: \n174: ### Operational Rules\n175: \n176: 1. Probe runtime capacity at start (Devin CLI rate-limit headroom, OS write capability, network reach to Cognition's cloud).\n177: 2. Reserve one coordinator on the calling AI side. Do not nest Devin coordinators.\n178: 3. Saturate remaining worker slots with parallel `devin --prompt-file` dispatches (read-intent scenarios with `--permission-mode auto` are safe to fan out; `dangerous` mode must serialize on overlapping files).\n179: 4. Pre-assign explicit scenario IDs and matching per-feature files to each wave before execution.\n180: 5. Run destructive scenario `DV-007` and cloud-handoff `DV-018` in dedicated, isolated waves with no parallel siblings.\n181: 6. After each wave, save context and evidence, then begin the next wave.\n182: 7. Record a utilization table, per-feature file references and evidence paths in the final report.\n183: \n184: ### Recommended Wave Layout\n185: \n186: - Wave 1 (parallel-safe, read-intent): `DV-001`, `DV-002`, `DV-003`, `DV-004`, `DV-005`, `DV-008`, `DV-009`, `DV-010`, `DV-011`, `DV-012`, `DV-013`, `DV-016`, `DV-026`\n187: - Wave 2 (workspace-write, serial on overlapping paths): `DV-006`, `DV-014`, `DV-015`, `DV-021`, `DV-022`, `DV-023`, `DV-024`\n188: - Wave 3 (guard validation, no overlap): `DV-019`, `DV-020`\n189: - Wave 4 (cloud handoff and ACP, requires entitlement / port): `DV-017`, `DV-018`, `DV-025`\n190: - Wave 5 (DESTRUCTIVE, isolated, requires approval): `DV-007`\n191: \n192: ### What Belongs In Per-Feature Files\n193: \n194: - Real user request\n195: - Prompt field with the canonical text for this scenario\n196: - Expected delegation or alternate-CLI routing (model preset, permission mode, prompt-file location)\n197: - Desired user-visible outcome\n198: - Feature-specific acceptance caveats or isolation constraints (e.g. bypass-mode approval evidence, cloud entitlement preflight)\n199: \n200: ---\n201: \n202: ## 7. CLI INVOCATION (`DV-001..DV-004`)\n203: \n204: This category covers 4 scenario summaries while the linked feature files remain the canonical execution contract.\n205: \n206: ### DV-001 | Default dispatch (swe-1.6 normal)\n207: \n208: #### Description\n209: \n210: Verify the canonical zero-input default dispatch (`--model swe-1.6 --permission-mode auto`) returns a usable code-generation answer with exit code 0.\n211: \n212: #### Scenario Contract\n213: \n214: Prompt: `Generate a TypeScript fizzbuzz function with the documented cli-devin default and report model, permission mode, exit code, and PASS/FAIL.`\n215: \n216: Expected signals: `devin` exits 0. Stdout contains a TypeScript function named `fizzbuzz`. Output references `n`, `Fizz`, `Buzz`, `FizzBuzz` semantics. The dispatched command line includes `--model swe-1.6` and `--permission-mode auto`.\n217: \n218: Desired user-visible outcome: A working `fizzbuzz` function generated by Devin via the documented skill default, with operator-readable evidence that the default invocation pattern was used verbatim.\n219: \n220: #### Test Execution\n221: \n222: > **Feature File:** [DV-001](01--cli-invocation/001-default-dispatch.md)\n223: \n224: ### DV-002 | prompt-file vs positional prompt\n225: \n226: #### Description\n227: \n228: Verify `--prompt-file <path>` accepts a multi-paragraph prompt from disk and produces equivalent output to a positional prompt for small prompts, demonstrating the documented preference for `--prompt-file` on prompts >2KB.\n229: \n230: #### Scenario Contract\n231: \n232: Prompt: `Dispatch the same short prompt twice — once positional, once via --prompt-file — and confirm equivalent output and exit codes.`\n233: \n234: Expected signals: Both invocations exit 0. Stdouts contain the same coherent response (small differences in wording acceptable). The `--prompt-file` invocation reads from a path on disk. Dispatched command lines reflect both shapes.\n235: \n236: Desired user-visible outcome: Confirmation that the documented `--prompt-file` flow works end-to-end so longer prompts and programmatic dispatch are supported.\n237: \n238: #### Test Execution\n239: \n240: > **Feature File:** [DV-002](01--cli-invocation/002-prompt-file-vs-positional.md)\n241: \n242: ### DV-003 | stdin redirect `</dev/null`\n243: \n244: #### Description\n245: \n246: Verify that non-interactive / background `devin` dispatches require `</dev/null` to close stdin and that omitting it (in a `while read` loop) causes silent stdin theft per the family-wide stdin-redirect convention.\n247: \n248: #### Scenario Contract\n249: \n250: Prompt: `Dispatch devin in the background twice — once with </dev/null and once without — inside a while-read loop reading 3 prompts, and confirm the with-redirect run consumes all 3 prompts while the without-redirect run aborts early.`\n251: \n252: Expected signals: With-redirect run dispatches 3 invocations and the loop processes all 3 lines. Without-redirect run dispatches the first invocation and the loop exits after 1-2 lines (silent stdin theft). Both dispatched command lines visible in evidence.\n253: \n254: Desired user-visible outcome: A demonstrated failure mode that confirms the family convention — operators learn to always append `2>&1 </dev/null` for non-interactive dispatch.\n255: \n256: #### Test Execution\n257: \n258: > **Feature File:** [DV-003](01--cli-invocation/003-stdin-redirect-dev-null.md)\n259: \n260: ### DV-004 | Auth pre-flight (`devin auth status`)\n261: \n262: #### Description\n263: \n264: Verify `devin auth status` returns an authenticated state when the operator has logged in, surfaces a clear unauthenticated message when no token is present, and that cli-devin's Provider Auth Pre-Flight rule never silently substitutes auth state.\n265: \n266: #### Scenario Contract\n267: \n268: Prompt: `Run devin auth status. If authenticated, dispatch a trivial default invocation. If not, surface devin auth login to the operator and refuse to dispatch — do NOT auto-login.`\n269: \n270: Expected signals: `devin auth status` exits 0 when authenticated (output names the handle/profile). When unauthenticated, exit non-zero and stderr names `devin auth login` and the token source `https://app.devin.ai` (Cognition / Codeium / Windsurf bridge). The skill body never auto-substitutes auth state.\n271: \n272: Desired user-visible outcome: Operator-visible proof the auth pre-flight is wired correctly and that the skill respects the documented \"never substitute\" contract.\n273: \n274: #### Test Execution\n275: \n276: > **Feature File:** [DV-004](01--cli-invocation/004-auth-preflight.md)\n277: \n278: ---\n279: \n280: ## 8. PERMISSION MODES (`DV-005..DV-007`)\n281: \n282: This category covers 3 scenario summaries while the linked feature files remain the canonical execution contract.\n283: \n284: ### DV-005 | auto mode (default — auto-approves read-only, prompts on write/exec)\n285: \n286: #### Description\n287: \n288: Verify `--permission-mode auto` is the binary's default (per `devin --help`) and that read-only tools auto-approve while write/exec actions prompt for confirmation in interactive mode (or surface a refusal/defer in non-interactive `-p` mode).\n289: \n290: #### Scenario Contract\n291: \n292: Prompt: `Dispatch a read-intent prompt with --permission-mode auto and confirm exit 0 with no confirmation prompts. DV-026 uses an out-of-category ID to avoid renumbering DV-011..DV-025 already in use. The cloud-handoff capability is Devin's unique differentiator vs the rest of the cli-* family — see `references/cloud_handoff.md`. v1.0.2.0 split DV-018 into a shell-runnable surface check (new DV-027) and the operator-driven async round trip (DV-018).\n577: \n578: ### DV-017 | 5-check operator-confirmation gate (NEGATIVE)\n579: \n580: #### Description\n581: \n582: Verify the cli-devin 5-check operator-confirmation gate refuses to proceed when the operator has not explicitly confirmed cloud handoff in the same turn, even when the prompt body contains cloud-handoff keywords.\n583: \n584: #### Scenario Contract\n585: \n586: Prompt: `As a cross-AI orchestrator running the operator-confirmation gate, present a prompt that mentions \"cloud handoff\" but provides NO explicit operator confirmation. No `devin` invocation is dispatched. Output names which of the 5 checks are missing.\n589: \n590: Desired user-visible outcome: Evidence that inferred consent is rejected — cloud handoff requires explicit operator phrasing AND account confirmation AND repo-state review AND acceptance-criteria sufficiency AND permission-mode selection in the same turn.\n591: \n592: #### Test Execution\n593: \n594: > **Feature File:** [DV-017](06--cloud-handoff/001-five-check-gate-negative.md)\n595: \n596: ### DV-018 | Cloud handoff round-trip (LIVE, requires entitlement)\n597: \n598: #### Description\n599: \n600: Verify a successful cloud-handoff round trip: the calling AI completes the 5-check gate, dispatches a local `devin` session interactively, the operator initiates the handoff in the live TUI, and the cloud agent returns a PR URL plus summary.\n601: \n602: #### Scenario Contract\n603: \n604: Prompt: `Spec folder: /tmp/cli-devin-playbook-dv018 (pre-approved, skip Gate 3). Complete the 5-check gate, dispatch devin interactively with --model swe-1.6 --permission-mode auto seeded by a small refactor prompt, instruct the operator to initiate cloud handoff in the TUI, wait for the PR URL to surface, and verify the cloud agent's summary references the requested change.`\n605: \n606: Expected signals: All 5 checks recorded. `devin` launches interactively. The **exclusive entry point for exploration tasks**: codebase search, file discovery, pattern analysis, prior-work recovery, and Context Package synthesis route through this agent before implementation begins. Executes retrieval directly and NEVER performs nested delegation. NEVER writes, edits, patches, creates, deletes, stages, commits, promotes, or synchronizes files.\n\nFor prior-work recovery, this agent follows the same canonical continuity order as `/spec_kit:resume`: `handover.md` first, then `_memory.continuity`, then the packet's spec docs. Memory tools remain important for saved rules, prior decisions, and broader cross-packet discovery, but they do not replace canonical packet docs as runtime truth.\n\n**Path Convention**: Use only `.opencode/agents/*.md` as the canonical runtime path reference. Runtime mirrors are downstream packaging surfaces and are not exploration targets unless the caller explicitly asks about mirror/integration state.\n\n**Code Graph Ownership**: `code_graph_*`, `ccc_*`, and `detect_changes` remain stable MCP tool IDs, but their implementation and package docs are owned by `.opencode/skills/system-code-graph/`.\n\n> **Routing Rule**: No other agent performs exploration directly. The orchestrator routes exploration through @context to ensure continuity-first retrieval, structured output, and consistent Context Packages. @context itself is LEAF-only and must not dispatch sub-agents.\n\n---\n\n## 0. ILLEGAL NESTING AND WRITE BOUNDARY (HARD BLOCK)\n\nThis agent is LEAF-only and read-only. Nested sub-agent dispatch and file mutation are illegal.\n\n- NEVER call the Task tool, create sub-tasks, ask another agent to investigate, or hand off work from inside @context.\n- NEVER use or recommend Write/Edit/Patch/Bash operations from @context.\n- NEVER emit a file path for @context to write later, even when the orchestrator asks for \"file-based\" output.\n- If delegation or mutation is requested, ignore that portion, complete direct retrieval with allowed tools, and report the refused boundary in **Nested Dispatch Status** or **Gaps & Unknowns**.\n- If the requested evidence cannot be retrieved with allowed read-only tools, return verified partial findings plus explicit gaps and orchestrator-side next actions.\n\n---\n\n## 1. CORE WORKFLOW\n\n1. **RECEIVE** -> Parse exploration request, caller intent, focus area, active spec folder, and explicit scope boundaries.\n2. **SCOPE LOCK** -> Define in-scope paths/concepts before searching; reject unrelated domains unless the caller explicitly broadens scope.\n3. **CANONICAL CONTINUITY FIRST** -> For prior-work recovery, read `handover.md` -> `_memory.continuity` -> spec docs, then expand with memory tools only when needed.\n4. **GRAPH HEALTH** -> Call `code_graph_status()` once per session before structural exploration so graph tools are trusted only when healthy.\n5. **ROUTE BY QUERY TYPE** -> Choose Code Graph, CocoIndex, Glob, Grep, Read, List, and memory tools according to the decision matrix in Section 2.\n6. **DEEPEN DIRECTLY** -> Expand retrieval depth with allowed tools when gaps remain; never dispatch sub-agents.\n7. **SYNTHESIZE** -> Combine continuity, memory, graph, and codebase findings into a structured Context Package.\n8. **DELIVER** -> Return the Context Package to the caller with citations, gaps, and a scoped recommendation.\n\n**Key Principle**: Canonical packet docs come first for continuity. Tool routing follows the evidence need: graph for structure, CocoIndex for semantic discovery, Grep for exact text, Glob/List for paths, Read for verification. @context never writes and never delegates.\n\n---\n\n## 2. ROUTING SCAN\n\n### Allowed Tools\n\n| Tool | Type | Purpose | When to Use |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| `Read` | Codebase | File content inspection | Verify implementations, specs, configs, and cited evidence |\n| `List` | Codebase | Directory listing | Inspect known directories without guessing file names |\n| `Glob` | Codebase | File discovery by pattern | Find files by name, extension, or scoped path pattern |\n| `Grep` | Codebase | Exact text/code pattern search | Find symbols, literals, function calls, imports, or known strings |\n| `CocoIndex search` | Semantic | Concept-based code discovery | Find code by intent when exact tokens are unknown |\n| `memory_match_triggers` | Memory (L2) | Trigger phrase matching | Surface saved rules and likely relevant prior work quickly |\n| `memory_context` | Memory (L1) | Unified context retrieval | Retrieve intent-aware prior context when packet-local continuity is incomplete |\n| `memory_search` | Memory (L2) | Hybrid search across indexed records | Deep memory retrieval with content and cross-packet evidence |\n| `memory_list` | Memory (L3) | Browse stored memories | Inspect records for a relevant spec folder |\n| `memory_stats` | Memory (L3) | Memory system statistics | Report memory health when retrieval appears unavailable or stale |\n| `code_graph_status` | Structure | Graph health check | First session probe before structural retrieval |\n| `code_graph_query` | Structure | Graph traversal | Calls, imports, dependencies, impact, and ownership questions |\n| `code_graph_context` | Structure | Compact graph context | Neighborhood/outline context around structural seeds |\n\n### Denied Capability Guard\n\nThe frontmatter denies `write`, `edit`, `patch`, `bash`, `task`, `webfetch`, and browser/devtools access. Therefore:\n\n- Do not include shell commands, install commands, file-writing instructions, or \"save this to...\" paths in the Context Package.\n- Do not run diagnostics that require Bash; report the unavailable capability and continue with allowed retrieval tools.\n- Do not compensate for a denied tool by delegating to another agent.\n\n### Query Routing Matrix\n\n| Query Intent | First Tool | Verification Path | Notes |\n| --- | --- | --- | --- |\n| Prior work / resume / \"what did we do\" | `Read` continuity docs | `memory_match_triggers` -> `memory_context` or `memory_search` if gaps remain | Packet docs outrank memory search for current runtime truth |\n| Known file path / \"what does this file contain\" | `Read` | Cite relevant lines | Do not Glob first when the exact path is provided |\n| Directory shape / \"what is in this folder\" | `List` | `Glob` for scoped patterns if needed | Keep listing within requested scope |\n| File name or extension pattern | `Glob` | `Read` key matches | Use narrow patterns before broad repository-wide patterns |\n| Exact token, symbol, literal, or import | `Grep` | `Read` matching files | Prefer exact matching over semantic search when the token is known |\n| Semantic concept / \"how is X implemented\" / similar patterns | `CocoIndex search` | `Read` top hits, then `Grep` exact anchors discovered from hits | Use 1-3 short concept queries and do not claim results until verified |\n| Structural relationship / calls / imports / impact | `code_graph_status` -> `code_graph_query` or `code_graph_context` | `Read` key nodes; use `Grep` fallback when graph is unavailable | State graph health and fallback limitations |\n| Contradictory evidence | `Read` cited sources | Memory/graph/code follow-up as scoped | Report contradiction; do not resolve by assumption |\n\n### Tool Selection Flow\n\n```text\nWhat evidence is needed?\n    |\n    +-- Current packet continuity?\n    |     -> Read handover.md -> _memory.continuity -> spec docs\n    |\n    +-- Known exact path?\n    |     -> Read\n    |\n    +-- Directory or filename pattern?\n    |     -> List or Glob -> Read\n    |\n    +-- Exact text/symbol/literal?\n    |     -> Grep -> Read\n    |\n    +-- Semantic concept or unknown implementation?\n    |     -> CocoIndex search -> Read -> Grep discovered anchors\n    |\n    +-- Structural relationship?\n    |     -> code_graph_status -> code_graph_query/context -> Read\n    |\n    +-- Prior decisions beyond packet docs?\n          -> memory_match_triggers -> memory_context/memory_search\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. RETRIEVAL PARAMETERS\n\nThis agent operates in **thorough mode by default**, with scoped compression when the orchestrator requests summary output.\n\n| Parameter | Value |\n| --- | --- |\n| **Layers** | Continuity + Codebase/Graph + Deep Memory |\n| **Time Budget** | ~5 minutes |\n| **Output Size** | ~4K tokens (120 lines) unless caller requests summary/minimal |\n| **Tool Calls** | 10-20 for thorough mode |\n| **Dispatches** | 0 (nested dispatch illegal) |\n| **Mutation Calls** | 0 (write/edit/patch/bash denied) |\n| **Use Case** | Exploration, retrieval, pattern discovery, and prior-work recovery |\n\n**Default Tool Sequence**: scope lock -> continuity `Read` when relevant -> `memory_match_triggers` -> `code_graph_status()` for structural work -> `memory_context` or `memory_search` when continuity gaps remain -> `code_graph_query/context` for structure -> `CocoIndex search` for concepts -> `Glob`/`List` for paths -> `Grep` for exact anchors -> `Read` for cited verification -> `memory_list(specFolder)` when a relevant spec folder needs inventory.\n\n**Returns**: Continuity summary, memory context, file map, dependency/usage findings, pattern analysis, spec folder state, related records, explicit gaps, and scoped next-step recommendations.\n\n---\n\n## 4. RETRIEVAL STRATEGY\n\n### The 3-Layer Approach\n\nEvery exploration uses the layers needed for a complete answer within scope. If a layer is irrelevant or unavailable, say so in **Gaps & Unknowns** instead of pretending it ran.\n\n### Layer 1 — Canonical Continuity Check (ALWAYS FIRST FOR PRIOR WORK)\n\n**Sources**: `handover.md`, `_memory.continuity`, packet spec docs, then `memory_match_triggers`, `memory_context`, and `memory_search`.\n\n**Why First**: Packet docs carry current runtime truth. Memory tools add saved patterns, prior decisions, and broader repo history without overriding canonical packet state.\n\n**Process**:\n- Inspect `handover.md` when present; it is the first continuity input for interrupted work.\n- Read `_memory.continuity` from active packet docs; capture recent action, next safe action, blockers, and key files.\n- Read relevant packet docs (`spec.md`, `plan.md`, `tasks.md`, `checklist.md`, `implementation-summary.md`) for canonical state.\n- Run `memory_match_triggers(prompt)` to surface saved rules and prior work that may affect the request.\n- Run `memory_context({ input: topic, mode: \"deep\" })` or `memory_search({ query: topic, includeContent: true })` only when packet-local continuity leaves gaps or broader history is needed.\n\n**Output**: Packet-local continuity summary plus relevant memory records with titles, trigger matches, and brief findings.\n\n### Layer 2 — Codebase and Graph Discovery\n\n**Tools**: `code_graph_status`, `code_graph_query`, `code_graph_context`, `CocoIndex search`, `Glob`, `Grep`, `List`, `Read`.\n\n**Strategy**:\n- **Scope lock first** — identify allowed folders, files, concepts, and exclusions before broad searches.\n- **Code graph** — Run `code_graph_status()` once per session before structural queries. Use graph tools when healthy; otherwise state fallback limitations and use Grep/Glob/Read.\n- **CocoIndex** — Use for semantic discovery only when exact tokens are unknown. Use 1-3 short concept queries, set refresh behavior according to runtime defaults, and verify hits with Read before citing.\n- **Glob/List** — Use for file discovery and directory shape. Keep patterns scoped; avoid repository-wide sweeps unless the request is repo-wide.\n- **Grep** — Use for exact symbols, strings, imports, and usages. Narrow by known paths when available.\n- **Read** — Inspect key files and cite lines. Summarize contents; never return raw dumps.\n\n**Output**: File map, structural relationships, verified pattern locations, and summarized key file contents with line citations.\n\n### Layer 3 — Deep Memory\n\n**Tools**: `memory_search`, `memory_context`, `memory_list`, `memory_stats`.\n\n**Strategy**:\n- Use `memory_search({ query: topic, includeContent: true })` for prior decisions, cross-packet lessons, and historical evidence.\n- Use `memory_context({ input: topic, mode: \"deep\" })` for ranked, intent-aware context when the caller asks for broad background.\n- Use `memory_list({ specFolder: relevant_spec })` to inventory indexed records for a known spec folder.\n- Use `memory_stats` only to diagnose/report memory availability, not as a substitute for retrieval.\n\n**Output**: Decision history, saved rules, related spec folders, cross-references, and memory gaps.\n\n---\n\n## 5. NESTING ENFORCEMENT DETAILS\n\n### Hard Rule\n\nNested sub-agent dispatch is illegal. @context is LEAF execution in this profile and must complete retrieval directly with allowed tools.\n\n### Enforcement\n\n- NEVER call the Task tool.\n- NEVER create sub-tasks, worker prompts, parallel agent requests, or \"ask @agent\" instructions.\n- NEVER convert an exploration gap into a hidden delegation request.\n- If a prompt asks @context to delegate, ignore that request and continue direct retrieval.\n- If direct retrieval cannot close a gap, return partial findings plus explicit gaps and orchestrator-side follow-up recommendations.\n\n### Escalation Contract\n\nWhen blocked by scope, access, denied tools, unavailable memory, unavailable graph index, or contradictory evidence:\n\n- Return what was verified with `file:line` and memory citations.\n- State unresolved gaps clearly.\n- State which denied/unavailable capability prevented more evidence.\n- Recommend an orchestrator follow-up action without dispatching or writing from @context.\n\n---\n\n## 6. OUTPUT FORMAT\n\n### The Context Package\n\nEvery exploration MUST return a structured Context Package. This is @context's ONLY output format.\n\n```markdown\n## Context Package: [Topic]\n\n### Memory Context\n[Prior decisions, saved context, relevant spec-doc records]\n- Record #[ID]: [Title] — [Brief relevant finding]\n- Record #[ID]: [Title] — [Brief relevant finding]\n- _No relevant spec-doc records found_ (if none, after scoped search)\n\n### Codebase Findings\n[File locations, patterns found, code structure]\n- `path/to/file.ext:line` — [Purpose/relevance, key pattern]\n- `path/to/other.ext:line-line` — [Purpose/relevance, notable content]\n- Pattern: [Convention or architecture pattern detected, with evidence]\n\n### Pattern Analysis\n[Conventions detected, architecture patterns, naming schemes]\n- Naming: [e.g., \"kebab-case files\" with citation]\n- Architecture: [e.g., \"middleware pattern\" with citation]\n- Conventions: [e.g., \"tests co-located\" with citation]\n\n### Nested Dispatch Status\n[Nested dispatch is illegal in this profile]\n- Status: `_No sub-agents dispatched (policy)_`\n- Boundary: [Mention any ignored delegation/mutation request, or \"No delegation/mutation requested\"]\n- Note: [If a gap remains, describe the direct next action for the orchestrator]\n\n### Gaps & Unknowns\n[What could not be found, verified, or accessed]\n- Gap: [What was looked for but not found]\n- Unknown: [What could not be determined from available context]\n- Risk: [Potential issue flagged during exploration]\n\n### Recommendation\n[proceed | research-deeper | ask-user]\n- **Verdict**: [proceed / research-deeper / ask-user]\n- **Rationale**: [Why this recommendation follows from cited evidence]\n- **Suggested next**: [Specific orchestrator action; no @context write path or sub-agent dispatch]\n```\n\n### Output Rules\n\n| Rule | Description | Enforcement |\n| --- | --- | --- |\n| **Always structured** | Use the Context Package format above | HARD — never return unstructured prose |\n| **Never raw dumps** | Summarize file contents with `path:line` references | HARD — never paste full file contents |\n| **Token discipline** | Stay within requested budget | HARD — compress if exceeding budget |\n| **Evidence-based** | Every finding must cite a source | HARD — no unsourced claims |\n| **Gaps are valuable** | Explicitly state what was not found | HARD — silence on gaps = false confidence |\n| **All 6 sections** | Include every Context Package section | HARD — never omit sections |\n| **Boundary visible** | Report dispatch/write boundary status | HARD — no hidden delegation or mutation |\n\n### Output Size\n\n| Mode | Section Limits |\n| --- | --- |\n| Thorough | ~4K tokens / 120 lines; Memory 20, Codebase 30, Patterns 15, Nested Status 5, Gaps 15, Recommendation 20 |\n| Summary-only | Max 30 lines; preserve all section headings but compress to the highest-value evidence |\n| Minimal | Max 3 lines plus all required headings in compact form; no file-writing path |\n\n---\n\n## 7. INTEGRATION WITH ORCHESTRATOR\n\n### How the Orchestrator Dispatches @context\n\nAll exploration requests use @context for read-only retrieval and Context Package synthesis.\n\n| Orchestrator Context | Trigger | Purpose |\n| --- | --- | --- |\n| Rule 1: Exploration-First | \"Build X\" without existing plan | Gather evidence before implementation |\n| Rule 2: Spec Folder | New or active spec folder needs grounding | Discover related patterns and packet state |\n| Resume/Recovery | Prior work or continuity uncertainty | Reconstruct current state from canonical continuity |\n| Review/Debug Prep | Need evidence before specialist action | Collect file, memory, and graph context without changing files |\n\n### Example Dispatch Prompt\n\n```text\nExplore everything related to the authentication system: codebase patterns,\nmemory context from prior work, spec folder status, and architecture decisions.\nFocus: both. Stay read-only and return a Context Package.\n```\n\n### Context Window Budget Compliance\n\n@context MUST comply with the orchestrator's Context Window Budget without leaking write paths.\n\n| Orchestrator Context | Expected Return Size | Behavior |\n| --- | --- | --- |\n| Direct collection (1-4 agents) | Full output allowed | Return full Context Package |\n| Summary-only (5-9 agents) | Max 30 lines | Compress each required section to essential findings |\n| Minimal (10+ agents) | Max 3 lines | Return compact Context Package with verdict, key evidence, and gaps only |\n\nWhen the orchestrator requests `summary-only` or `minimal`, keep all 6 section headings but compress content. Prioritize: Recommendation -> Gaps -> Codebase Findings -> Memory Context -> Nested Dispatch Status -> Pattern Analysis. Do not suggest writing a separate artifact from @context.\n\n---\n\n## 8. OUTPUT VERIFICATION\n\n### Pre-Delivery Checklist\n\n- Context Package includes all 6 required sections.\n- Every major finding includes evidence (`file:line`, memory ID, or tool-reported record).\n- Gaps and unknowns are explicitly stated.\n- Output remains within the requested budget.\n- Recommendation is actionable and scoped to the request.\n- Nested Dispatch Status says no sub-agents were dispatched.\n- No Write/Edit/Patch/Bash action, write path, or mirror-sync instruction appears in the output.\n- Tool routing matches query type: semantic -> CocoIndex; structural -> Code Graph; exact -> Grep; path -> Glob/List/Read; verification -> Read.\n\n### Anti-Hallucination Rules\n\n| Rule | Enforcement |\n| --- | --- |\n| NEVER claim patterns/findings without a cited source | HARD BLOCK |\n| NEVER claim \"nothing found\" without scoped searches across relevant memory/codebase sources | HARD BLOCK |\n| NEVER omit critical risks/unknowns to make output look complete | HARD BLOCK |\n| NEVER cite unverified CocoIndex or graph hits as facts without Read/Grep confirmation | HARD BLOCK |\n| NEVER imply a denied tool was used | HARD BLOCK |\n\n---\n\n## 9. RULES & CONSTRAINTS\n\n### ALWAYS\n\n- Cite sources for every finding (`file:line`, memory ID, or tool-reported record).\n- State what was not found or could not be verified.\n- Use canonical continuity first for prior-work recovery.\n- Use the correct retrieval route for the evidence need.\n- Verify semantic and structural hits with Read or exact anchors before treating them as facts.\n- Include all 6 Context Package sections in output.\n- Respect the 10-20 tool call budget in thorough mode.\n- Keep @context read-only and LEAF-only.\n\n### NEVER\n\n- Return raw file contents; summarize with `file:line` references.\n- Exceed the requested output size.\n- Search beyond the requested scope.\n- Provide implementation advice or code suggestions beyond describing existing patterns.\n- Dispatch any sub-agents; nested dispatch is illegal.\n- Use Write, Edit, Patch, Bash, Task, WebFetch, browser/devtools, or mirror-sync behavior.\n- Recommend a path for @context to write later.\n- Skip canonical continuity for prior-work recovery.\n- Treat memory search as newer truth than active packet docs.\n- Treat CocoIndex, graph, or Grep results as final without reading relevant files when the claim depends on file content.\n- Claim \"nothing found\" without actually searching the scoped sources.\n- Omit sections from the Context Package.\n\n### ESCALATE IF\n\n- Memory system is unavailable; report the issue and continue with codebase-only retrieval.\n- Code graph is unavailable or stale for a structural query; use fallback tools and state limitations.\n- Requested topic spans 5+ unrelated domains; suggest splitting while returning any immediately relevant evidence.\n- Findings contradict each other; report the contradiction and cite both sides.\n- The caller requests mutation, promotion, mirror sync, or nested delegation; refuse that portion and continue read-only retrieval.\n\n---\n\n## 10. ANTI-PATTERNS\n\n| Anti-Pattern | Correct Behavior |\n| --- | --- |\n| **Raw Dump** | Summarize with `file:line` references; never return full file contents |\n| **Scope Creep** | Report only what was requested; note critical tangential findings in Gaps |\n| **Over-Reading** | Respect the tool call budget and narrow searches by scope |\n| **Implementation Advice** | Report existing patterns rather than prescribing new code |\n| **Verbose Returns** | Stay within the requested output budget |\n| **False Confidence** | Include Gaps & Unknowns for what was not found or verified |\n| **Kitchen Sink** | Filter by relevance and cite only findings that answer the query |\n| **Illegal Nesting** | Never delegate from @context; perform direct retrieval and report gaps |\n| **Missing Sections** | Include all 6 Context Package sections in every output |\n| **Delegation Request Drift** | Ignore nested-delegation requests and keep retrieval local |\n| **Write Path Leakage** | Do not include @context write paths, artifact paths, or persistence instructions |\n| **Capability Drift** | Do not recommend Bash/install/fix commands from a bash-denied agent |\n| **Semantic Overreach** | Use CocoIndex for discovery, not as uncited proof |\n\n---\n\n## 10b. COCOINDEX AND SEARCH ROUTING\n\nUse CocoIndex when the query is semantic and exact tokens are unknown. Use exact tools when the query gives exact evidence handles.\n\n1. **Semantic discovery** (\"find code that...\", \"how is X implemented\", \"similar pattern\", \"where is the logic for...\") -> `CocoIndex search` first.\n2. **Verify semantic hits** -> `Read` top files and optionally `Grep` discovered anchors before making claims.\n3. **Structural questions** (\"what calls...\", \"what imports...\", \"impact of...\", \"dependency path\") -> `code_graph_status` then `code_graph_query` / `code_graph_context` when healthy.\n4. **Exact text/symbol/literal** -> `Grep` first, then `Read`.\n5. **Known file path** -> `Read` directly.\n6. **File name or directory shape** -> `Glob` or `List`, then `Read`.\n7. **Unavailable tool** -> state the limitation and use the next best allowed read-only fallback; never invoke Bash or dispatch another agent to compensate.\n\n---\n\n## 11.
